2. Technology Stack Decisions
2.1. Frontend
 * Web Application:
   * Framework: React.js (or Next.js for SSR/SSG benefits). React offers a vast ecosystem, strong community support, and component-based development.
   * State Management: React Query (for data fetching and caching) and Zustand (for simpler global state). Redux is powerful but can be overkill for many applications.
   * Styling: Tailwind CSS (utility-first CSS framework for rapid UI development) combined with headless UI components (e.g., Headless UI, Radix UI) for accessibility.
   * Bundler: Vite (for fast development server and build times).
 * Mobile Applications (iOS/Android):
   * Framework: React Native. Allows for a single codebase for both platforms, leveraging React knowledge. This accelerates development and reduces maintenance.
   * Native Modules (for AR/VR integration): Will likely require writing some native Swift/Kotlin code for deep ARKit/ARCore integration, exposed to React Native via bridges.
2.2. Backend
 * Core Backend Language/Framework: Node.js with NestJS.
   * Node.js: Excellent for I/O-bound tasks, highly scalable, large community.
   * NestJS: A progressive Node.js framework for building efficient, reliable, and scalable server-side applications. It leverages TypeScript and provides an opinionated structure, ideal for microservices.
 * API Gateway: Kong Gateway (open-source, highly performant, API management layer) or AWS API Gateway (if deploying heavily on AWS for serverless options).
 * Databases:
   * Primary Relational Database: PostgreSQL. Robust, ACID-compliant, excellent for complex queries and transactional data (user profiles, orders, product details, CMS content).
   * Cache: Redis. For session management, frequently accessed data caching (e.g., popular strains, user recommendations for quick retrieval), and rate limiting.
   * Search Database/Engine: Elasticsearch. For full-text search capabilities on strains, products, articles, and dispensaries. Integrates well with Kibana for monitoring.
   * Graph Database (Potential Future): Neo4j (if complex relationships between effects, terpenes, cannabinoids, and conditions become a core recommendation feature requiring graph traversals).
 * Message Broker: Apache Kafka (or RabbitMQ for simpler needs). For asynchronous communication between microservices (e.g., order processing events, user activity for recommendations, notifications).
 * File Storage: AWS S3 / Google Cloud Storage. For images (product photos, 3D model textures), lab reports, and other static assets.
 * Containerization: Docker. For packaging microservices and their dependencies into portable containers.
 * Orchestration: Kubernetes. For deploying, scaling, and managing containerized applications across a cluster of machines.
 * Cloud Provider: AWS (Amazon Web Services) or Google Cloud Platform (GCP). Both offer comprehensive suites of services for compute, storage, databases, AI/ML, and networking. AWS is generally more mature and has more services, while GCP excels in AI/ML and Kubernetes integration. Let's assume AWS for this design due to its widespread adoption and breadth of services.
2.3. AI Module
 * Language: Python. The dominant language for AI/ML.
 * Machine Learning Frameworks: TensorFlow and/or PyTorch. For building, training, and deploying deep learning models (e.g., for recommendation engines, NLP for sentiment analysis).
 * ML Libraries: Scikit-learn (for classical ML algorithms), Pandas (data manipulation), NumPy (numerical operations).
 * MLOps Platform: AWS SageMaker. Provides tools for building, training, and deploying ML models at scale, including managed Jupyter notebooks, model registries, and deployment endpoints. MLflow for experiment tracking and model versioning.
 * Feature Store: Feast (open-source) or a custom solution built on Redis/PostgreSQL. For serving features to ML models consistently in both training and inference.
2.4. AR/VR Module
 * Development Platform: Unity 3D.
   * Why Unity: Industry-standard for interactive 3D content, strong community, vast asset store, cross-platform deployment (iOS, Android, VR headsets like Oculus/Meta Quest).
   * AR SDKs: ARFoundation (Unity's unified API for ARKit and ARCore), enabling cross-platform AR development.
   * VR SDKs: Oculus Integration (for Meta Quest), OpenXR (for broader VR headset support).
 * 3D Modeling Software: Blender (open-source, powerful for creating and exporting 3D assets).
 * Asset Storage & Delivery: AWS S3 (for storing 3D models and textures) combined with AWS CloudFront (CDN) for fast global delivery to AR/VR clients.
 * Interactivity: C# scripting within Unity.
2.5. E-commerce Module
 * Platform (Highly Dependent on Regulation):
   * Given the cannabis industry's high regulation, a highly customizable and compliant platform is needed.
   * Custom Microservice (built with NestJS/Node.js): This offers the most control over compliance logic, age verification, and integration with specific cannabis-friendly payment processors and seed-to-sale tracking systems (e.g., Metrc API integration in regulated states). This would be the most robust long-term solution.
   * Alternatively, a "headless" e-commerce solution with custom integrations: Platforms like BigCommerce or Magento (Adobe Commerce) offer strong APIs. However, compliance layers would still need to be built on top. Qredible Q-Transact is specifically designed for regulated industries.
 * Payment Gateway: Requires integration with cannabis-friendly payment processors. These are highly specific to region and vary. Solutions might involve ACH, specific high-risk merchant accounts, or even crypto if permitted. (e.g., Hypur, PayQwick, or a custom solution with a financial partner).
 * Tax Calculation: Avalara or TaxJar (APIs for real-time tax calculations, critical for varying cannabis taxes).
 * Inventory/Order Management: Managed within the custom e-commerce microservice, potentially integrating with existing ERP/seed-to-sale systems used by dispensaries.
2.6. PoD (Print-on-Demand) Module
 * Integration with Providers: Direct API integration with Printful and Printify. These handle the product catalog, order fulfillment, and shipping.
2.7. Voice Module
 * Speech-to-Text (STT): Google Cloud Speech-to-Text API or AWS Transcribe. High accuracy and scalability.
 * Natural Language Understanding (NLU): Google Dialogflow (for intent recognition and entity extraction) or Rasa (open-source framework for building conversational AI).
 * Text-to-Speech (TTS): Google Cloud Text-to-Speech API or AWS Polly. For generating natural-sounding voice responses.
 * Voice Activity Detection (VAD): Handled by mobile SDKs or integrated into the STT service.
 * Frontend Integration: Mobile apps will use native microphone APIs to capture audio, then send to the voice service.
2.8. 3D PoD Module
 * Integration with Providers: Direct API integration with Shapeways or Sculpteo.
 * 3D Viewer: Three.js or Babylon.js (JavaScript libraries for rendering 3D graphics in web browsers, for interactive previews).
 * Model Storage: AWS S3.
3. Component Interaction & Communication
 * API Gateway: All external requests from frontend applications (web, mobile, AR/VR) will go through the API Gateway. It handles:
   * Authentication & Authorization: Verifies user tokens (JWT) and ensures they have permission to access the requested service.
   * Rate Limiting: Protects backend services from abuse.
   * Routing: Directs requests to the appropriate microservice.
   * Load Balancing: Distributes traffic evenly among service instances.
 * Inter-service Communication:
   * Synchronous: RESTful APIs (HTTP/JSON) for most direct service-to-service calls (e.g., User Service requesting Product Service for product details).
   * Asynchronous: Kafka for event-driven communication.
     * Examples:
       * User completes an order (E-commerce Service publishes order.created event to Kafka).
       * Recommendation Service consumes order.created events to update user preferences and generate new recommendations.
       * Notification Service consumes various events (e.g., order.status_updated, new.recommendation_available) to send notifications.
       * AI Module publishes recommendations.generated events.
 * Data Flow for Recommendations:
   * Frontend sends user preferences/history to User Service.
   * User Service stores data in Auth Database and publishes user activity events to Kafka.
   * Recommendation Service (Python ML service) consumes user activity events from Kafka.
   * Recommendation Service retrieves product/strain data from Product Service (or its replica/cache).
   * ML models process data, generate recommendations, and store them in its own cache/database, and potentially publish recommendations.generated events to Kafka.
   * Frontend requests recommendations from Recommendation Service via API Gateway.
4. Infrastructure & Deployment (AWS Focus)
 * Compute:
   * AWS EKS (Elastic Kubernetes Service): Managed Kubernetes for deploying and scaling microservices.
   * AWS Lambda: For serverless functions for specific, event-driven tasks (e.g., image resizing after upload, triggering ML model retraining).
 * Networking:
   * Amazon VPC (Virtual Private Cloud): Isolated network environment.
   * AWS Load Balancer (ALB): Distributes incoming traffic.
   * AWS Route 53: DNS management.
   * AWS CloudFront: Content Delivery Network (CDN) for fast delivery of static assets (images, JS/CSS bundles, 3D models).
 * Monitoring & Logging:
   * AWS CloudWatch: For metrics, logs, and alarms.
   * Prometheus & Grafana: For custom metrics and dashboards within Kubernetes.
   * ELK Stack (Elasticsearch, Logstash, Kibana): For centralized log aggregation and analysis.
 * CI/CD (Continuous Integration/Continuous Delivery):
   * GitHub Actions / GitLab CI / AWS CodePipeline.
   * Automated testing, building Docker images, deploying to EKS.
 * Security:
   * AWS IAM (Identity and Access Management): For granular access control.
   * AWS WAF (Web Application Firewall): To protect against common web exploits.
   * AWS Secrets Manager: For securely storing API keys, database credentials.
   * SSL/TLS: End-to-end encryption.
   * Regular Security Audits & Penetration Testing.
   * Compliance Tools: Potentially leveraging AWS services that assist with HIPAA or other regulatory frameworks (though cannabis-specific compliance often requires specialized solutions).
5. Data Governance & Compliance
 * Strict Age Verification: Integrated into user onboarding and e-commerce.
 * Geo-fencing/Location-Based Services: To ensure compliance with local cannabis laws (e.g., restricting sales/delivery to legal jurisdictions).
 * "Seed-to-Sale" Tracking Integration: If direct sales are involved, integration with state-mandated systems (e.g., Metrc API in the US). This is a critical legal requirement.
 * Data Privacy: Adherence to GDPR, CCPA, and other relevant data privacy regulations for user data.
 * Disclaimers & Educational Content: Prominently displayed to ensure responsible use and legal awareness.

 * Database design:
General Conventions:
 * Table Names: Plural, snake_case (e.g., users, products).
 * Column Names: Singular, snake_case (e.g., user_id, product_name).
 * Primary Keys (PK): id (auto-incrementing BIGSERIAL for scalability).
 * Foreign Keys (FK): [referenced_table]_id (e.g., user_id referencing users.id).
 * Timestamps: created_at and updated_at (with TIMESTAMPTZ and defaults).
 * Enums: PostgreSQL's ENUM type can be very useful for predefined lists (e.g., strain_type, unit_of_measure).
 * JSONB: For flexible, schemaless data that might change frequently (e.g., user preferences with varying attributes, product metadata).
 Database Schema: potgrowhub_db
1. users Table
Stores core user information.
| Column Name | Data Type | Constraints | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| id | BIGSERIAL | PRIMARY KEY | Unique identifier for the user |
| username | VARCHAR(50) | NOT NULL, UNIQUE | User's chosen username |
| email | VARCHAR(255) | NOT NULL, UNIQUE | User's email address |
| password_hash | VARCHAR(255) | NOT NULL | Hashed password for security |
| full_name | VARCHAR(255) | NULLABLE | User's full name |
| date_of_birth | DATE | NOT NULL (for age verification) | User's date of birth |
| phone_number | VARCHAR(20) | UNIQUE | User's phone number (optional) |
| profile_picture_url | TEXT | NULLABLE | URL to user's profile picture |
| bio | TEXT | NULLABLE | Short user biography |
| location_country | VARCHAR(100) | NULLABLE | User's country (for geo-compliance) |
| location_state | VARCHAR(100) | NULLABLE | User's state/province (for geo-compliance) |
| user_type | ENUM('consumer', 'retailer', 'admin', 'moderator') | NOT NULL, DEFAULT 'consumer' | Role of the user in the system |
| is_active | BOOLEAN | NOT NULL, DEFAULT TRUE | Account status |
| last_login_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NULLABLE | Timestamp of last login |
| created_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() | Record creation timestamp |
| updated_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() | Last update timestamp (using ON UPDATE CURRENT_TIMESTAMP) |
2. user_preferences Table
Stores personalized settings and preferences for recommendations.
| Column Name | Data Type | Constraints | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| id | BIGSERIAL | PRIMARY KEY | Unique identifier for the preference record |
| user_id | BIGINT | NOT NULL, FK (users.id) | Foreign key to the users table |
| preference_key | VARCHAR(100) | NOT NULL | E.g., 'desired_effects', 'medical_conditions', 'flavor_profile' |
| preference_value | TEXT | NOT NULL | E.g., 'relaxation', 'anxiety_relief', 'citrus' |
| metadata | JSONB | NULLABLE | Additional preference details (e.g., 'intensity': 'high') |
| created_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() | Record creation timestamp |
| updated_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() | Last update timestamp |
| UNIQUE(user_id, preference_key, preference_value) | Composite Unique Constraint | Prevents duplicate preference entries for a user |  |
 * Note: For more complex, structured preferences, this could be denormalized or split into more specific tables (e.g., user_medical_conditions, user_desired_effects). JSONB offers flexibility here.
3. retailers Table
Stores information about dispensaries or cannabis retailers.
| Column Name | Data Type | Constraints | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| id | BIGSERIAL | PRIMARY KEY | Unique identifier for the retailer |
| user_id | BIGINT | NOT NULL, UNIQUE, FK (users.id) | Link to the user account managing this retailer profile (if applicable) |
| name | VARCHAR(255) | NOT NULL, UNIQUE | Retailer's business name |
| license_number | VARCHAR(100) | NOT NULL, UNIQUE | Official state/provincial license number |
| address_street | VARCHAR(255) | NOT NULL | Street address |
| address_city | VARCHAR(100) | NOT NULL | City |
| address_state | VARCHAR(100) | NOT NULL | State/province |
| address_zip_code | VARCHAR(20) | NOT NULL | Zip/postal code |
| address_country | VARCHAR(100) | NOT NULL | Country |
| latitude | NUMERIC(10,7) | NULLABLE | Latitude for geolocation |
| longitude | NUMERIC(10,7) | NULLABLE | Longitude for geolocation |
| phone_number | VARCHAR(20) | NULLABLE | Retailer's contact phone number |
| email | VARCHAR(255) | NULLABLE | Retailer's contact email |
| website_url | TEXT | NULLABLE | Retailer's website URL |
| operating_hours | JSONB | NULLABLE | E.g., { "mon": "9am-8pm", "tue": "9am-8pm", ... } |
| logo_url | TEXT | NULLABLE | URL to retailer's logo |
| description | TEXT | NULLABLE | Retailer's description |
| is_verified | BOOLEAN | NOT NULL, DEFAULT FALSE | Whether the retailer's license/details are verified |
| created_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() |  |
| updated_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() |  |
4. categories Table
Hierarchical categories for products, strains, articles.
| Column Name | Data Type | Constraints | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| id | BIGSERIAL | PRIMARY KEY | Unique identifier for the category |
| name | VARCHAR(100) | NOT NULL, UNIQUE | Category name (e.g., 'Flower', 'Edibles', 'Indica') |
| slug | VARCHAR(100) | NOT NULL, UNIQUE | URL-friendly slug (e.g., 'flower', 'edibles') |
| description | TEXT | NULLABLE | Category description |
| parent_id | BIGINT | NULLABLE, FK (categories.id) | For hierarchical categories (e.g., 'Indica' parent of 'Sativa') |
| created_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() |  |
| updated_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() |  |

| slug | VARCHAR(100) | NOT NULL, UNIQUE | URL-friendly slug |

Detailed information about cannabis strains.

| thc_max | NUMERIC(5,2) | NULLABLE | Maximum THC percentage |
| cbd_min | NUMERIC(5,2) | NULLABLE | Minimum CBD percentage |
| cbd_max | NUMERIC(5,2) | NULLABLE | Maximum CBD percentage |
| cbn_min | NUMERIC(5,2) | NULLABLE | Minimum CBN percentage |
| cbn_max | NUMERIC(5,2) | NULLABLE | Maximum CBN percentage |
| aroma_profile | TEXT | NULLABLE | Description of aroma/flavor profile |
| image_urls | TEXT[] | NULLABLE | Array of URLs for strain images |
| medical_uses_summary | TEXT | NULLABLE | Summary of common medical applications |
| cultivation_notes | TEXT | NULLABLE | Notes on growing the strain (optional) |
| created_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() |  |
| updated_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() |  |

| is_verified_purchase | BOOLEAN | NOT NULL, DEFAULT FALSE | If the review is from a confirmed purchase |
| created_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() |  |
| updated_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() |  |
| CHECK ( (strain_id IS NOT NULL AND product_id IS NULL AND retailer_id IS NULL) OR (product_id IS NOT NULL AND strain_id IS NULL AND retailer_id IS NULL) OR (retailer_id IS NOT NULL AND strain_id IS NULL AND product_id IS NULL) ) | Constraint: Only one foreign key can be set | Ensures review is for one type of entity |  |

| tracking_number | VARCHAR(100) | NULLABLE | Shipping tracking number |

19. recommendation_logs Table
Stores data for the AI module to learn from user interactions.
| Column Name | Data Type | Constraints | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| id | BIGSERIAL | PRIMARY KEY | Unique identifier for the log entry |
| user_id | BIGINT | NOT NULL, FK (users.id) | User who received/interacted with the recommendation |
| recommended_item_id | BIGINT | NOT NULL | ID of the item that was recommended |
| item_type | ENUM('strain', 'product', 'article') | NOT NULL | Type of item recommended |
| recommendation_source | VARCHAR(100) | NULLABLE | E.g., 'collaborative_filtering', 'content_based', 'popular' |
| interaction_type | ENUM('view', 'click', 'add_to_cart', 'purchase', 'rate') | NOT NULL | Type of interaction with the recommended item |
| rating_given | SMALLINT | NULLABLE | If interaction_type is 'rate' |
| context_data | JSONB | NULLABLE | Additional context, e.g., 'time_of_day', 'symptoms_at_time_of_recommendation' |
| logged_at | TIMESTAMPTZ | NOT NULL, DEFAULT NOW() | Timestamp of the interaction |
Important Considerations for PostgreSQL Specifics:
 * Enums: Define these custom types:
   CREATE TYPE strain_type AS ENUM ('indica', 'sativa', 'hybrid');
CREATE TYPE user_type AS ENUM ('consumer', 'retailer', 'admin', 'moderator');
CREATE TYPE order_status AS ENUM ('pending', 'confirmed', 'processing', 'shipped', 'delivered', 'cancelled', 'refunded');
CREATE TYPE payment_status AS ENUM ('paid', 'pending', 'failed', 'refunded');
CREATE TYPE delivery_type AS ENUM ('delivery', 'pickup');
CREATE TYPE article_status AS ENUM ('draft', 'published', 'archived');
CREATE TYPE item_type AS ENUM ('strain', 'product', 'article');
CREATE TYPE interaction_type AS ENUM ('view', 'click', 'add_to_cart', 'purchase', 'rate');
CREATE TYPE pod_product_type AS ENUM ('2d_print', '3d_print');

 * Indexes: Crucial for performance. Add indexes on:
   * All id (PKs are automatically indexed).
   * All FOREIGN KEY columns (e.g., user_id, product_id, retailer_id, category_id, tag_id, strain_id, order_id).
   * Frequently queried columns (e.g., username, email, name, status, created_at, published_at).
   * For JSONB columns where specific keys are frequently queried, consider GIN indexes.
   * For search, consider pg_trgm extension for trigram indexes on text fields.
 * Full-Text Search: For articles.content, strains.description, products.description, consider PostgreSQL's built-in full-text search capabilities using TSVECTOR and TSQUERY or integrating with Elasticsearch.
 * UUIDs: Instead of BIGSERIAL for id, you could use UUID for distributed systems, but BIGSERIAL with a centralized database (like a single PostgreSQL instance or a clustered setup) is generally fine and performs well.
 * Data Validation: While the database schema enforces data types and constraints, further validation should be done at the application layer.
 * Security: Never store raw passwords. Use strong hashing algorithms (e.g., bcrypt) and store only the hash.

 * Extensive coding : 
 * Frontend (React Web): User registration UI & API call.
 * Backend (NestJS): User Authentication API, Strain Data API, Product Data API, Recommendation API endpoint.
 * AI (Python/FastAPI): Simple Recommendation Model (pseudo-code) served via FastAPI.
 * Database Interactions (TypeORM in NestJS, SQLAlchemy in Python): CRUD for Users, Strains, Products.
1. Frontend Module (React Web)
Goal: User Registration Form and interaction with the Backend API.
Tech: React, Axios (for HTTP requests), Tailwind CSS (for styling).
src/components/RegisterForm.jsx
import React, { useState } from 'react';
import axios from 'axios';

function RegisterForm() {
    const [username, setUsername] = useState('');
    const [email, setEmail] = useState('');
    const [password, setPassword] = useState('');
    const [confirmPassword, setConfirmPassword] = useState('');
    const [dateOfBirth, setDateOfBirth] = useState('');
    const [locationState, setLocationState] = useState('');
    const [error, setError] = useState('');
    const [success, setSuccess] = useState('');

    const handleSubmit = async (e) => {
        e.preventDefault();
        setError('');
        setSuccess('');

        if (password !== confirmPassword) {
            setError('Passwords do not match.');
            return;
        }

        try {
            const response = await axios.post('http://localhost:3000/api/auth/register', {
                username,
                email,
                password,
                dateOfBirth, // Ensure format is YYYY-MM-DD
                locationState,
                userType: 'consumer', // Default for registration form
            });
            setSuccess('Registration successful! Please log in.');
            // Clear form
            setUsername('');
            setEmail('');
            setPassword('');
            setConfirmPassword('');
            setDateOfBirth('');
            setLocationState('');
        } catch (err) {
            console.error('Registration error:', err.response ? err.response.data : err.message);
            setError(err.response?.data?.message || 'Registration failed. Please try again.');
        }
    };

    return (
        <div className="min-h-screen flex items-center justify-center bg-gradient-to-br from-green-700 to-green-900 p-4">
            <div className="bg-white p-8 rounded-lg shadow-xl w-full max-w-md">
                <h2 className="text-3xl font-bold text-center text-green-800 mb-6">Register for GanjaGuru</h2>
                <form onSubmit={handleSubmit} className="space-y-4">
                    {error && <p className="text-red-600 text-center">{error}</p>}
                    {success && <p className="text-green-600 text-center">{success}</p>}

                    <div>
                        <label className="block text-gray-700 text-sm font-bold mb-2" htmlFor="username">
                            Username:
                        </label>
                        <input
                            type="text"
                            id="username"
                            className="shadow appearance-none border rounded w-full py-2 px-3 text-gray-700 leading-tight focus:outline-none focus:shadow-outline"
                            value={username}
                            onChange={(e) => setUsername(e.target.value)}
                            required
                        />
                    </div>
                    <div>
                        <label className="block text-gray-700 text-sm font-bold mb-2" htmlFor="email">
                            Email:
                        </label>
                        <input
                            type="email"
                            id="email"
                            className="shadow appearance-none border rounded w-full py-2 px-3 text-gray-700 leading-tight focus:outline-none focus:shadow-outline"
                            value={email}
                            onChange={(e) => setEmail(e.target.value)}
                            required
                        />
                    </div>
                    <div>
                        <label className="block text-gray-700 text-sm font-bold mb-2" htmlFor="password">
                            Password:
                        </label>
                        <input
                            type="password"
                            id="password"
                            className="shadow appearance-none border rounded w-full py-2 px-3 text-gray-700 leading-tight focus:outline-none focus:shadow-outline"
                            value={password}
                            onChange={(e) => setPassword(e.target.value)}
                            required
                        />
                    </div>
                    <div>
                        <label className="block text-gray-700 text-sm font-bold mb-2" htmlFor="confirmPassword">
                            Confirm Password:
                        </label>
                        <input
                            type="password"
                            id="confirmPassword"
                            className="shadow appearance-none border rounded w-full py-2 px-3 text-gray-700 leading-tight focus:outline-none focus:shadow-outline"
                            value={confirmPassword}
                            onChange={(e) => setConfirmPassword(e.target.value)}
                            required
                        />
                    </div>
                    <div>
                        <label className="block text-gray-700 text-sm font-bold mb-2" htmlFor="dateOfBirth">
                            Date of Birth:
                        </label>
                        <input
                            type="date"
                            id="dateOfBirth"
                            className="shadow appearance-none border rounded w-full py-2 px-3 text-gray-700 leading-tight focus:outline-none focus:shadow-outline"
                            value={dateOfBirth}
                            onChange={(e) => setDateOfBirth(e.target.value)}
                            required
                        />
                    </div>
                    <div>
                        <label className="block text-gray-700 text-sm font-bold mb-2" htmlFor="locationState">
                            State/Province:
                        </label>
                        <input
                            type="text"
                            id="locationState"
                            className="shadow appearance-none border rounded w-full py-2 px-3 text-gray-700 leading-tight focus:outline-none focus:shadow-outline"
                            value={locationState}
                            onChange={(e) => setLocationState(e.target.value)}
                            required
                        />
                    </div>
                    <button
                        type="submit"
                        className="w-full bg-green-600 hover:bg-green-700 text-white font-bold py-2 px-4 rounded focus:outline-none focus:shadow-outline transition duration-200"
                    >
                        Register
                    </button>
                </form>
            </div>
        </div>
    );
}

export default RegisterForm;

2. Backend Module (NestJS)
Goal: User Authentication (Register, Login), Strain & Product Management, and a Recommendation Proxy.
Tech: NestJS, TypeORM, PostgreSQL, bcryptjs, JWT.
src/users/user.entity.ts (TypeORM Entity)
import { Entity, PrimaryGeneratedColumn, Column, CreateDateColumn, UpdateDateColumn } from 'typeorm';

export enum UserType {
  CONSUMER = 'consumer',
  RETAILER = 'retailer',
  ADMIN = 'admin',
  MODERATOR = 'moderator',
}

@Entity('users')
export class User {
  @PrimaryGeneratedColumn('increment')
  id: number;

  @Column({ length: 50, unique: true, nullable: false })
  username: string;

  @Column({ length: 255, unique: true, nullable: false })
  email: string;

  @Column({ length: 255, nullable: false })
  passwordHash: string; // Storing hashed password

  @Column({ name: 'full_name', length: 255, nullable: true })
  fullName: string;

  @Column({ name: 'date_of_birth', type: 'date', nullable: false })
  dateOfBirth: Date;

  @Column({ name: 'phone_number', length: 20, unique: true, nullable: true })
  phoneNumber: string;

  @Column({ name: 'profile_picture_url', type: 'text', nullable: true })
  profilePictureUrl: string;

  @Column({ type: 'text', nullable: true })
  bio: string;

  @Column({ name: 'location_country', length: 100, nullable: true })
  locationCountry: string;

  @Column({ name: 'location_state', length: 100, nullable: true })
  locationState: string;

  @Column({
    type: 'enum',
    enum: UserType,
    default: UserType.CONSUMER,
    nullable: false,
  })
  userType: UserType;

  @Column({ name: 'is_active', type: 'boolean', default: true, nullable: false })
  isActive: boolean;

  @Column({ name: 'last_login_at', type: 'timestamptz', nullable: true })
  lastLoginAt: Date;

  @CreateDateColumn({ name: 'created_at', type: 'timestamptz', default: () => 'CURRENT_TIMESTAMP' })
  createdAt: Date;

  @UpdateDateColumn({ name: 'updated_at', type: 'timestamptz', default: () => 'CURRENT_TIMESTAMP' })
  updatedAt: Date;
}

src/auth/auth.controller.ts (Authentication Endpoints)
import { Controller, Post, Body, HttpCode, HttpStatus, UseGuards, Request } from '@nestjs/common';
import { AuthService } from './auth.service';
import { RegisterDto } from './dto/register.dto';
import { LoginDto } from './dto/login.dto';
import { LocalAuthGuard } from './guards/local-auth.guard'; // Assuming you set up LocalAuthGuard for login

@Controller('auth')
export class AuthController {
  constructor(private authService: AuthService) {}

  @Post('register')
  @HttpCode(HttpStatus.CREATED)
  async register(@Body() registerDto: RegisterDto) {
    const user = await this.authService.register(registerDto);
    // Remove sensitive data before returning
    const { passwordHash, ...result } = user;
    return result;
  }

  @Post('login')
  @HttpCode(HttpStatus.OK)
  @UseGuards(LocalAuthGuard) // Uses Passport.js LocalStrategy for initial user validation
  async login(@Request() req) { // req.user is populated by LocalAuthGuard
    // The LocalAuthGuard already validated the user, now generate JWT
    return this.authService.login(req.user);
  }

  // Example of a protected route
  // @UseGuards(JwtAuthGuard)
  // @Get('profile')
  // getProfile(@Request() req) {
  //   return req.user;
  // }
}

src/auth/auth.service.ts (Authentication Logic)
import { Injectable, ConflictException, UnauthorizedException, BadRequestException } from '@nestjs/common';
import { InjectRepository } from '@nestjs/typeorm';
import { Repository } from 'typeorm';
import { User, UserType } from '../users/user.entity';
import * as bcrypt from 'bcrypt';
import { JwtService } from '@nestjs/jwt';
import { RegisterDto } from './dto/register.dto';
import { LoginDto } from './dto/login.dto';

@Injectable()
export class AuthService {
  constructor(
    @InjectRepository(User)
    private usersRepository: Repository<User>,
    private jwtService: JwtService,
  ) {}

  async register(registerDto: RegisterDto): Promise<User> {
    const { username, email, password, dateOfBirth, locationState, userType } = registerDto;

    // Basic age verification (example: must be 21 or older)
    const dob = new Date(dateOfBirth);
    const ageDiffMs = Date.now() - dob.getTime();
    const ageDate = new Date(ageDiffMs);
    const age = Math.abs(ageDate.getUTCFullYear() - 1970);
    if (age < 21) {
        throw new BadRequestException('You must be at least 21 years old to register.');
    }

    const existingUserByEmail = await this.usersRepository.findOne({ where: { email } });
    if (existingUserByEmail) {
      throw new ConflictException('Email already in use.');
    }

    const existingUserByUsername = await this.usersRepository.findOne({ where: { username } });
    if (existingUserByUsername) {
      throw new ConflictException('Username already taken.');
    }

    const passwordHash = await bcrypt.hash(password, 10); // Salt rounds: 10

    const newUser = this.usersRepository.create({
      username,
      email,
      passwordHash,
      dateOfBirth: dob,
      locationState,
      locationCountry: 'United States', // Assuming default for now
      userType: userType || UserType.CONSUMER, // Default to consumer if not specified
      isActive: true,
    });

    return this.usersRepository.save(newUser);
  }

  async validateUser(email: string, pass: string): Promise<any> {
    const user = await this.usersRepository.findOne({ where: { email } });
    if (user && await bcrypt.compare(pass, user.passwordHash)) {
      // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-unused-vars
      const { passwordHash, ...result } = user;
      return result;
    }
    return null;
  }

  async login(user: any) {
    const payload = { username: user.username, sub: user.id, userType: user.userType };
    // Update last login timestamp
    await this.usersRepository.update(user.id, { lastLoginAt: new Date() });
    return {
      access_token: this.jwtService.sign(payload),
      user: { id: user.id, username: user.username, email: user.email, userType: user.userType }, // Return basic user info
    };
  }
}

(Note: This needs AuthModule, JwtModule, LocalStrategy setup for Passport.js, and DTOs. Omitted for brevity.)
src/strains/strains.controller.ts (Strain API Endpoints)
import { Controller, Get, Post, Body, Param, Put, Delete, Query, UseGuards } from '@nestjs/common';
import { StrainsService } from './strains.service';
import { CreateStrainDto } from './dto/create-strain.dto';
import { UpdateStrainDto } from './dto/update-strain.dto';
import { JwtAuthGuard } from '../auth/guards/jwt-auth.guard'; // Assuming JWT protection
import { RolesGuard } from '../auth/guards/roles.guard'; // For RBAC
import { Roles } from '../auth/decorators/roles.decorator'; // For RBAC

@Controller('strains')
export class StrainsController {
  constructor(private readonly strainsService: StrainsService) {}

  @Post()
  @UseGuards(JwtAuthGuard, RolesGuard)
  @Roles('admin', 'moderator') // Only admins/moderators can create strains
  create(@Body() createStrainDto: CreateStrainDto) {
    return this.strainsService.create(createStrainDto);
  }

  @Get()
  findAll(@Query('search') search?: string, @Query('type') type?: string, @Query('limit') limit?: number) {
    return this.strainsService.findAll(search, type, limit);
  }

  @Get(':slug')
  findOne(@Param('slug') slug: string) {
    return this.strainsService.findOneBySlug(slug);
  }

  @Put(':id')
  @UseGuards(JwtAuthGuard, RolesGuard)
  @Roles('admin', 'moderator')
  update(@Param('id') id: string, @Body() updateStrainDto: UpdateStrainDto) {
    return this.strainsService.update(+id, updateStrainDto);
  }

  @Delete(':id')
  @UseGuards(JwtAuthGuard, RolesGuard)
  @Roles('admin') // Only admins can delete strains
  remove(@Param('id') id: string) {
    return this.strainsService.remove(+id);
  }
}

src/strains/strains.service.ts (Strain Database Interactions)
import { Injectable, NotFoundException } from '@nestjs/common';
import { InjectRepository } from '@nestjs/typeorm';
import { Like, Repository } from 'typeorm';
import { Strain } from './strain.entity'; // Assuming Strain entity
import { CreateStrainDto } from './dto/create-strain.dto';
import { UpdateStrainDto } from './dto/update-strain.dto';
import slugify from 'slugify'; // npm install slugify

@Injectable()
export class StrainsService {
  constructor(
    @InjectRepository(Strain)
    private strainsRepository: Repository<Strain>,
  ) {}

  async create(createStrainDto: CreateStrainDto): Promise<Strain> {
    const slug = slugify(createStrainDto.name, { lower: true, strict: true });
    const newStrain = this.strainsRepository.create({ ...createStrainDto, slug });
    return this.strainsRepository.save(newStrain);
  }

  async findAll(search?: string, type?: string, limit?: number): Promise<Strain[]> {
    const queryBuilder = this.strainsRepository.createQueryBuilder('strain');

    if (search) {
      queryBuilder.where('LOWER(strain.name) LIKE LOWER(:search)', { search: `%${search}%` })
                  .orWhere('LOWER(strain.description) LIKE LOWER(:search)', { search: `%${search}%` });
    }

    if (type) {
      queryBuilder.andWhere('strain.strainType = :type', { type });
    }

    if (limit) {
        queryBuilder.limit(limit);
    }

    return queryBuilder.getMany();
  }

  async findOne(id: number): Promise<Strain> {
    const strain = await this.strainsRepository.findOne({ where: { id } });
    if (!strain) {
      throw new NotFoundException(`Strain with ID ${id} not found`);
    }
    return strain;
  }

  async findOneBySlug(slug: string): Promise<Strain> {
    const strain = await this.strainsRepository.findOne({ where: { slug } });
    if (!strain) {
      throw new NotFoundException(`Strain with slug "${slug}" not found`);
    }
    return strain;
  }

  async update(id: number, updateStrainDto: UpdateStrainDto): Promise<Strain> {
    const strain = await this.strainsRepository.preload({ id: id, ...updateStrainDto });
    if (!strain) {
      throw new NotFoundException(`Strain with ID ${id} not found`);
    }
    // Update slug if name changes
    if (updateStrainDto.name && strain.name !== updateStrainDto.name) {
        strain.slug = slugify(updateStrainDto.name, { lower: true, strict: true });
    }
    return this.strainsRepository.save(strain);
  }

  async remove(id: number): Promise<void> {
    const result = await this.strainsRepository.delete(id);
    if (result.affected === 0) {
      throw new NotFoundException(`Strain with ID ${id} not found`);
    }
  }
}

src/recommendations/recommendations.controller.ts (Recommendation Proxy/Endpoint)
import { Controller, Get, Query, UseGuards, Req } from '@nestjs/common';
import { JwtAuthGuard } from '../auth/guards/jwt-auth.guard';
import { RecommendationService } from './recommendation.service';

@Controller('recommendations')
@UseGuards(JwtAuthGuard) // Protect this endpoint
export class RecommendationsController {
  constructor(private readonly recommendationService: RecommendationService) {}

  @Get('personalized')
  async getPersonalizedRecommendations(
    @Req() req,
    @Query('type') type?: 'strain' | 'product',
    @Query('limit') limit: number = 5,
  ) {
    const userId = req.user.id; // User ID from JWT payload
    return this.recommendationService.getPersonalizedRecommendations(userId, type, limit);
  }

  @Get('trending')
  async getTrendingRecommendations(
    @Query('type') type?: 'strain' | 'product',
    @Query('limit') limit: number = 10,
  ) {
    return this.recommendationService.getTrendingRecommendations(type, limit);
  }
}

src/recommendations/recommendation.service.ts (Recommendation Service - calling AI Microservice)
import { Injectable, InternalServerErrorException } from '@nestjs/common';
import axios from 'axios';
import { ConfigService } from '@nestjs/config'; // For accessing environment variables

@Injectable()
export class RecommendationService {
  private readonly aiServiceUrl: string;

  constructor(private configService: ConfigService) {
    this.aiServiceUrl = this.configService.get<string>('AI_SERVICE_URL');
  }

  async getPersonalizedRecommendations(
    userId: number,
    type: 'strain' | 'product',
    limit: number,
  ) {
    try {
      // Call the AI microservice for personalized recommendations
      const response = await axios.get(`${this.aiServiceUrl}/recommendations/personalized`, {
        params: {
          user_id: userId,
          item_type: type,
          limit: limit,
        },
      });
      return response.data;
    } catch (error) {
      console.error('Error fetching personalized recommendations from AI service:', error.response?.data || error.message);
      throw new InternalServerErrorException('Could not retrieve personalized recommendations.');
    }
  }

  async getTrendingRecommendations(
    type: 'strain' | 'product',
    limit: number,
  ) {
    try {
      // Call the AI microservice for trending items (no user ID needed)
      const response = await axios.get(`${this.aiServiceUrl}/recommendations/trending`, {
        params: {
          item_type: type,
          limit: limit,
        },
      });
      return response.data;
    } catch (error) {
      console.error('Error fetching trending recommendations from AI service:', error.response?.data || error.message);
      throw new InternalServerErrorException('Could not retrieve trending recommendations.');
    }
  }
}

3. AI Module (Python/FastAPI)
Goal: Provide a simple personalized recommendation endpoint.
Tech: Python, FastAPI, Pandas, a dummy ML model (or placeholder logic).
ai_service/main.py
from fastapi import FastAPI, HTTPException
from pydantic import BaseModel
from typing import List, Optional
import pandas as pd
import random

app = FastAPI(
    title="GanjaGuru AI Recommendation Service",
    description="Provides personalized and trending recommendations for strains and products.",
    version="0.1.0",
)

# --- Dummy Data (Replace with actual database interaction/feature store lookup) ---
# In a real scenario, this would come from the Product/Strain services or a data lake
dummy_strains = [
    {"id": 101, "name": "Blue Dream", "type": "hybrid", "effects": ["uplifting", "relaxing"]},
    {"id": 102, "name": "OG Kush", "type": "indica", "effects": ["sleepy", "euphoric"]},
    {"id": 103, "name": "Sour Diesel", "type": "sativa", "effects": ["energetic", "creative"]},
    {"id": 104, "name": "Granddaddy Purple", "type": "indica", "effects": ["sleepy", "pain relief"]},
    {"id": 105, "name": "Amnesia Haze", "type": "sativa", "effects": ["focus", "happy"]},
]

dummy_products = [
    {"id": 201, "name": "CBD Gummies (10mg)", "type": "edible", "effects": ["calming"]},
    {"id": 202, "name": "THC Vape Cart (Sativa)", "type": "vape", "effects": ["energetic"]},
    {"id": 203, "name": "Relaxing Balm", "type": "topical", "effects": ["localized relief"]},
]

# Simulate user preferences/history
# In reality, this would be fetched from `user_preferences` and `recommendation_logs` tables
dummy_user_profiles = {
    1: {"preferred_effects": ["relaxing", "sleepy"], "disliked_effects": ["energetic"]},
    2: {"preferred_effects": ["energetic", "creative"], "disliked_effects": ["sleepy"]},
}

# --- Pydantic Models for Request/Response ---
class RecommendationRequest(BaseModel):
    user_id: Optional[int] = None
    item_type: Optional[str] = None # 'strain' or 'product'
    limit: int = 5

class RecommendedItem(BaseModel):
    id: int
    name: str
    type: str
    effects: List[str]
    source: str # e.g., 'personalized', 'trending'

# --- Recommendation Logic (Simplified for demonstration) ---
def get_personalized_items_logic(user_id: int, item_type: str, limit: int):
    user_profile = dummy_user_profiles.get(user_id)
    if not user_profile:
        # Fallback to trending or general popular items if no profile
        return get_trending_items_logic(item_type, limit, "personalized_fallback")

    preferred_effects = set(user_profile.get("preferred_effects", []))
    disliked_effects = set(user_profile.get("disliked_effects", []))

    all_items = []
    if item_type == "strain" or item_type is None:
        all_items.extend(dummy_strains)
    if item_type == "product" or item_type is None:
        all_items.extend(dummy_products)

    # Simple scoring: prioritize items with preferred effects, penalize disliked
    scored_items = []
    for item in all_items:
        score = 0
        item_effects = set(item.get("effects", []))
        if item_effects.intersection(preferred_effects):
            score += 10
        if item_effects.intersection(disliked_effects):
            score -= 5
        scored_items.append((score, item))

    # Sort by score (descending) and then randomly select to add variety
    scored_items.sort(key=lambda x: x[0], reverse=True)
    
    # Simple selection from top 2x candidates to add some randomness
    top_candidates = [item for score, item in scored_items if score > -5][:limit*2]
    
    # Shuffle and pick limit items
    random.shuffle(top_candidates)
    
    return [
        RecommendedItem(
            id=item["id"],
            name=item["name"],
            type=item["type"],
            effects=item["effects"],
            source="personalized"
        ) for item in top_candidates[:limit]
    ]

def get_trending_items_logic(item_type: str, limit: int, source_prefix=""):
    items = []
    if item_type == "strain" or item_type is None:
        items.extend(dummy_strains)
    if item_type == "product" or item_type is None:
        items.extend(dummy_products)

    # Simulate trending by simply shuffling and taking a slice
    random.shuffle(items)
    
    final_source = "trending"
    if source_prefix:
        final_source = f"{source_prefix}_{final_source}"

    return [
        RecommendedItem(
            id=item["id"],
            name=item["name"],
            type=item["type"],
            effects=item["effects"],
            source=final_source
        ) for item in items[:limit]
    ]


# --- FastAPI Endpoints ---
@app.get("/recommendations/personalized", response_model=List[RecommendedItem])
async def get_personalized_recommendations(
    user_id: int,
    item_type: Optional[str] = None,
    limit: int = 5
):
    """
    Returns personalized strain or product recommendations for a given user.
    """
    if not user_id:
        raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="User ID is required for personalized recommendations.")
    
    if item_type not in ['strain', 'product', None]:
        raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="Invalid item_type. Must be 'strain', 'product', or empty.")

    recommendations = get_personalized_items_logic(user_id, item_type, limit)
    return recommendations

@app.get("/recommendations/trending", response_model=List[RecommendedItem])
async def get_trending_recommendations(
    item_type: Optional[str] = None,
    limit: int = 10
):
    """
    Returns trending strain or product recommendations.
    """
    if item_type not in ['strain', 'product', None]:
        raise HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="Invalid item_type. Must be 'strain', 'product', or empty.")

    recommendations = get_trending_items_logic(item_type, limit)
    return recommendations

if __name__ == "__main__":
    import uvicorn
    # To run: uvicorn main:app --reload --port 8001
    uvicorn.run(app, host="0.0.0.0", port=8001)
4. Database Interactions (SQL/TypeORM for Backend, Conceptual for AI)
We've already seen TypeORM in the NestJS examples. Here's a brief look at conceptual SQL and how the AI might interact with data.
Sample SQL for Database Setup (PostgreSQL)
-- Create ENUM types first
CREATE TYPE user_type AS ENUM ('consumer', 'retailer', 'admin', 'moderator');
CREATE TYPE strain_type AS ENUM ('indica', 'sativa', 'hybrid');
CREATE TYPE order_status AS ENUM ('pending', 'confirmed', 'processing', 'shipped', 'delivered', 'cancelled', 'refunded');
CREATE TYPE payment_status AS ENUM ('paid', 'pending', 'failed', 'refunded');
CREATE TYPE delivery_type AS ENUM ('delivery', 'pickup');
CREATE TYPE article_status AS ENUM ('draft', 'published', 'archived');
CREATE TYPE item_type AS ENUM ('strain', 'product', 'article');
CREATE TYPE interaction_type AS ENUM ('view', 'click', 'add_to_cart', 'purchase', 'rate');
CREATE TYPE pod_product_type AS ENUM ('2d_print', '3d_print');


-- users Table
CREATE TABLE users (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    username VARCHAR(50) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    email VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    password_hash VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    full_name VARCHAR(255),
    date_of_birth DATE NOT NULL,
    phone_number VARCHAR(20) UNIQUE,
    profile_picture_url TEXT,
    bio TEXT,
    location_country VARCHAR(100),
    location_state VARCHAR(100),
    user_type user_type NOT NULL DEFAULT 'consumer',
    is_active BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,
    last_login_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- retailers Table
CREATE TABLE retailers (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    user_id BIGINT UNIQUE REFERENCES users(id),
    name VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    license_number VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    address_street VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    address_city VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL,
    address_state VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL,
    address_zip_code VARCHAR(20) NOT NULL,
    address_country VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL,
    latitude NUMERIC(10,7),
    longitude NUMERIC(10,7),
    phone_number VARCHAR(20),
    email VARCHAR(255),
    website_url TEXT,
    operating_hours JSONB,
    logo_url TEXT,
    description TEXT,
    is_verified BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- categories Table
CREATE TABLE categories (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    slug VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    description TEXT,
    parent_id BIGINT REFERENCES categories(id),
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- tags Table
CREATE TABLE tags (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    slug VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    type VARCHAR(50),
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- strains Table
CREATE TABLE strains (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    slug VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    strain_type strain_type NOT NULL,
    description TEXT,
    lineage TEXT,
    thc_min NUMERIC(5,2),
    thc_max NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbd_min NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbd_max NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbn_min NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbn_max NUMERIC(5,2),
    aroma_profile TEXT,
    image_urls TEXT[],
    medical_uses_summary TEXT,
    cultivation_notes TEXT,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- strain_terpenes Table
CREATE TABLE strain_terpenes (
    strain_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES strains(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
    terpene_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES terpenes(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
    percentage NUMERIC(5,2),
    PRIMARY KEY (strain_id, terpene_id)
);

-- terpenes Table
CREATE TABLE terpenes (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    description TEXT,
    aroma VARCHAR(255),
    medical_benefits TEXT,
    image_url TEXT,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- products Table
CREATE TABLE products (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    retailer_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES retailers(id),
    name VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    slug VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    description TEXT,
    category_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES categories(id),
    strain_id BIGINT REFERENCES strains(id),
    brand VARCHAR(100),
    price NUMERIC(10,2) NOT NULL,
    currency VARCHAR(3) NOT NULL DEFAULT 'USD',
    thc_content NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbd_content NUMERIC(5,2),
    unit_of_measure VARCHAR(50),
    quantity_per_unit NUMERIC(10,2),
    inventory_count INTEGER,
    image_urls TEXT[],
    lab_test_url TEXT,
    is_available BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,
    metadata JSONB,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    UNIQUE (retailer_id, slug)
);

-- product_tags Table
CREATE TABLE product_tags (
    product_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES products(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
    tag_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES tags(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
    PRIMARY KEY (product_id, tag_id)
);

-- reviews Table
CREATE TABLE reviews (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    user_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES users(id),
    strain_id BIGINT REFERENCES strains(id),
    product_id BIGINT REFERENCES products(id),
    retailer_id BIGINT REFERENCES retailers(id),
    rating SMALLINT NOT NULL CHECK (rating >= 1 AND rating <= 5),
    title VARCHAR(255),
    comment TEXT,
    effects_felt TEXT[],
    symptoms_helped TEXT[],
    is_verified_purchase BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    CHECK ( (strain_id IS NOT NULL AND product_id IS NULL AND retailer_id IS NULL) OR
            (product_id IS NOT NULL AND strain_id IS NULL AND retailer_id IS NULL) OR
            (retailer_id IS NOT NULL AND strain_id IS NULL AND product_id IS NULL) )
);

-- recommendation_logs Table (for AI training data)
CREATE TABLE recommendation_logs (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    user_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES users(id),
    recommended_item_id BIGINT NOT NULL,
    item_type item_type NOT NULL,
    recommendation_source VARCHAR(100),
    interaction_type interaction_type NOT NULL,
    rating_given SMALLINT CHECK (rating_given >= 1 AND rating_given <= 5),
    context_data JSONB,
    logged_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- Add indexes where appropriate
CREATE INDEX idx_users_email ON users(email);
CREATE INDEX idx_users_username ON users(username);
CREATE INDEX idx_retailers_name ON retailers(name);
CREATE INDEX idx_strains_name ON strains(name);
CREATE INDEX idx_products_name ON products(name);
CREATE INDEX idx_reviews_user_id ON reviews(user_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_reviews_strain_id ON reviews(strain_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_reviews_product_id ON reviews(product_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_reviews_retailer_id ON reviews(retailer_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_recommendation_logs_user_id ON recommendation_logs(user_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_recommendation_logs_item_type ON recommendation_logs(item_type);

5. AR/VR Module (Conceptual Unity C# Component)
Goal: Load a 3D model of a cannabis bud/plant and display basic info.
Tech: Unity 3D (C#), calls to Backend API for data.
Assets/Scripts/CannabisBudLoader.cs
using UnityEngine;
using System.Collections;
using System.Collections.Generic;
using UnityEngine.Networking; // For HTTP requests
using SimpleJSON; // A simple JSON parsing library, or use Unity's JsonUtility/Newtonsoft.Json

public class CannabisBudLoader : MonoBehaviour
{
    public string strainSlug = "blue-dream"; // Set in Inspector or passed dynamically
    public GameObject budPrefab; // Assign your 3D bud model prefab in the Inspector
    public TextMesh infoTextPrefab; // Assign a TextMesh Pro prefab for info display

    private string baseUrl = "http://localhost:3000/api/strains/"; // Your NestJS backend URL
    private GameObject currentBudInstance;
    private TextMesh currentInfoText;

    void Start()
    {
        if (budPrefab == null)
        {
            Debug.LogError("Bud Prefab is not assigned in the Inspector!");
            return;
        }
        if (infoTextPrefab == null)
        {
            Debug.LogError("Info Text Prefab is not assigned in the Inspector!");
            return;
        }

        StartCoroutine(FetchStrainDataAndLoadModel(strainSlug));
    }

    IEnumerator FetchStrainDataAndLoadModel(string slug)
    {
        string uri = baseUrl + slug;
        using (UnityWebRequest webRequest = UnityWebRequest.Get(uri))
        {
            // Optional: Add authorization header if API is protected
            // webRequest.SetRequestHeader("Authorization", "Bearer YOUR_JWT_TOKEN");

            yield return webRequest.SendWebRequest();

            if (webRequest.result == UnityWebRequest.Result.ConnectionError || webRequest.result == UnityWebRequest.Result.ProtocolError)
            {
                Debug.LogError("Error fetching strain data: " + webRequest.error);
            }
            else
            {
                Debug.Log("Strain Data Received: " + webRequest.downloadHandler.text);
                ParseStrainData(webRequest.downloadHandler.text);
            }
        }
    }

    void ParseStrainData(string jsonString)
    {
        // Using SimpleJSON for quick parsing. In a real project, use proper data models/JsonUtility.
        var N = JSON.Parse(jsonString);

        string strainName = N["name"].Value;
        string description = N["description"].Value;
        string type = N["strainType"].Value;
        string thcMin = N["thcMin"].Value;
        string thcMax = N["thcMax"].Value;
        string cbdMin = N["cbdMin"].Value;
        string cbdMax = N["cbdMax"].Value;
        string imageUrl = N["imageUrls"][0].Value; // Assuming the first URL is the main 3D model/texture

        // Instantiate the 3D model
        if (currentBudInstance != null) Destroy(currentBudInstance);
        currentBudInstance = Instantiate(budPrefab, transform.position, Quaternion.identity, transform);
        currentBudInstance.transform.localScale = Vector3.one * 0.1f; // Adjust size

        // Load texture if available (more complex for actual 3D models)
        if (!string.IsNullOrEmpty(imageUrl))
        {
            StartCoroutine(LoadTextureIntoModel(currentBudInstance, imageUrl));
        }

        // Display information
        if (currentInfoText != null) Destroy(currentInfoText.gameObject);
        currentInfoText = Instantiate(infoTextPrefab, transform.position + new Vector3(0, 0.2f, 0), Quaternion.identity, transform);
        currentInfoText.text = $"<b>{strainName} ({type})</b>\nTHC: {thcMin}-{thcMax}%\nCBD: {cbdMin}-{cbdMax}%\n\n{description.Substring(0, Mathf.Min(description.Length, 150))}...";
        currentInfoText.fontSize = 0.05f; // Adjust font size
        currentInfoText.characterSize = 0.5f; // Adjust visual size
        currentInfoText.transform.localScale = Vector3.one; // Keep text scale normal
        currentInfoText.transform.LookAt(Camera.main.transform); // Make text always face camera
        currentInfoText.transform.Rotate(0, 180, 0); // Correct for typical TextMesh orientation
    }

    IEnumerator LoadTextureIntoModel(GameObject model, string url)
    {
        UnityWebRequest request = UnityWebRequestTexture.GetTexture(url);
        yield return request.SendWebRequest();

        if (request.result == UnityWebRequest.Result.Success)
        {
            Texture2D texture = DownloadHandlerTexture.GetContent(request);
            if (model.GetComponent<Renderer>() != null)
            {
                // Assign to the main material of the model's renderer
                model.GetComponent<Renderer>().material.mainTexture = texture;
            }
            else
            {
                // If it's a complex model with multiple renderers (e.g., child objects)
                foreach (Renderer r in model.GetComponentsInChildren<Renderer>())
                {
                    r.material.mainTexture = texture;
                }
            }
            Debug.Log($"Texture loaded for {model.name}");
        }
        else
        {
            Debug.LogError($"Failed to load texture from {url}: {request.error}");
        }
    }

    void Update()
    {
        // Simple rotation for visualization
        if (currentBudInstance != null)
        {
            currentBudInstance.transform.Rotate(Vector3.up * 20f * Time.deltaTime);
        }
        // Ensure info text always faces camera in AR/VR
        if (currentInfoText != null && Camera.main != null)
        {
            currentInfoText.transform.LookAt(Camera.main.transform);
            currentInfoText.transform.Rotate(0, 180, 0);
        }
    }
}

How to Run/Test these snippets (Conceptual Steps):
 * Database: Set up a PostgreSQL database instance and apply the provided SQL schema.
 * Backend:
   * Create a new NestJS project (nest new ganja-guru-backend).
   * Install dependencies: npm install @nestjs/typeorm pg bcryptjs @nestjs/jwt passport @nestjs/passport @passport-local jwt-decode slugify
   * Configure AppModule with TypeOrmModule.forRoot() pointing to your PostgreSQL.
   * Create the User entity, AuthModule, StrainsModule, RecommendationsModule and import them into AppModule.
   * Ensure JWT secret is set in .env (e.g., JWT_SECRET=yoursecretkey) and AI_SERVICE_URL=http://localhost:8001
   * Run npm run start:dev.
 * AI Module:
   * Create a new Python virtual environment (python -m venv venv).
   * Activate it (source venv/bin/activate or .\venv\Scripts\activate).
   * Install dependencies: pip install fastapi uvicorn pandas pydantic
   * Navigate to the ai_service directory and run uvicorn main:app --reload --port 8001.
 * Frontend:
   * Create a new React project (npx create-react-app ganja-guru-frontend or npm create vite@latest).
   * Install dependencies: npm install axios tailwindcss postcss autoprefixer. Configure Tailwind.
   * Place RegisterForm.jsx in src/components.
   * Update App.js to render <RegisterForm />.
   * Run npm start.
 * AR/VR:
   * Open Unity Hub, create a new 3D project.
   * Install ARFoundation, ARCore XR Plugin, ARKit XR Plugin via Window > Package Manager.
   * Import a simple 3D bud model (e.g., a .fbx or .obj file) into your Assets, create a prefab from it.
   * Create a new C# script CannabisBudLoader.cs and paste the code.
   * Create an empty GameObject in your scene, name it "BudLoader" and attach the CannabisBudLoader script.
   * Drag your bud prefab and a TextMesh Pro prefab (or standard TextMesh if TMP isn't set up) to the corresponding slots in the Inspector.
   * Adjust camera for AR setup if going mobile, or just run in editor for desktop visualization.

 * Dependency management:
Overarching Principles:
 * Strict Versioning: Pin dependencies to exact versions where possible (package-lock.json, yarn.lock, Pipfile.lock, go.mod). Use semantic versioning for updates (major, minor, patch).
 * Regular Auditing: Periodically check for known vulnerabilities using built-in tools (e.g., npm audit, pip audit) and third-party services.
 * Automated Updates (Controlled): Set up a process (e.g., Dependabot, RenovateBot) to suggest and automate dependency updates, but require CI/CD checks and human review for major/minor versions.
 * Private Package Hosting: For internal libraries or sensitive dependencies, use private registries (e.g., JFrog Artifactory, Nexus Repository Manager, GitHub Packages).
 * Environment Isolation: Ensure development, testing, and production environments use consistent dependencies.
 * Documentation: Clearly document dependency choices and any workarounds for compatibility issues.
Module-Specific Dependency Management:
1. Frontend (Web & Mobile - React/React Native)
 * Package Manager: npm (Node Package Manager) or Yarn.
   * Recommendation: Start with npm for its widespread adoption and package-lock.json for deterministic builds. If specific features like workspaces or faster installs become critical, consider Yarn.
 * Configuration Files:
   * package.json: Defines project metadata, scripts, and direct dependencies (dependencies for runtime, devDependencies for build tools/testing).
   * package-lock.json: Automatically generated by npm, locks down the exact versions of all dependencies (direct and transitive) to ensure reproducible builds. This file should always be committed to version control.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * React (web): react, react-dom
   * React Native (mobile): react-native
   * Navigation: react-navigation/native-stack
   * State Management: @tanstack/react-query, zustand
   * UI Libraries: tailwindcss (with postcss, autoprefixer), @headlessui/react (or radix-ui)
   * Form Handling: react-hook-form
   * HTTP Client: axios or fetch
   * Build Tools: vite (for React web), metro (for React Native)
   * Testing: jest, @testing-library/react (or native)
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * Semantic Versioning (npm): Use ^ for minor-version compatibility during initial development, but once a stable version is found for a dependency, consider pinning to exact versions (1.2.3) or using ~ (patch compatibility) for critical libraries to prevent unexpected breaking changes. The package-lock.json is the primary mechanism for exact reproducibility.
   * React Native CLI/Expo: Be mindful of the React Native version and its compatibility with native modules. Follow their release cycles and upgrade guides. Expo manages a lot of this automatically, simplifying things.
   * Native Module Linking (React Native): Use npx react-native autolink (or equivalent) for native modules. Carefully manage Podfile.lock (iOS) and build.gradle (Android) for native dependencies.
2. Backend (Node.js with NestJS)
 * Package Manager: npm or Yarn.
   * Recommendation: Same as frontend, stick with npm for consistency and its package-lock.json.
 * Configuration Files:
   * package.json: Defines direct dependencies (@nestjs/common, @nestjs/platform-express, typeorm, pg etc.), devDependencies (@types/node, @nestjs/cli).
   * package-lock.json: Essential for locking down exact versions for reproducible server builds.
   * tsconfig.json: TypeScript configuration, ensuring compatibility between TypeScript versions and library types.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * NestJS Core: @nestjs/core, @nestjs/common
   * Platform: @nestjs/platform-express
   * Database ORM/Query Builder: typeorm or prisma
   * Database Driver: pg (for PostgreSQL)
   * Validation: class-validator, class-transformer
   * Authentication: @nestjs/jwt, passport
   * HTTP Client: axios
   * Message Broker Client: kafkajs (for Kafka) or amqplib (for RabbitMQ)
   * Testing: jest, supertest
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * NestJS Ecosystem: NestJS is quite opinionated and updates frequently. Follow their release notes and ensure all @nestjs/* packages are on compatible versions.
   * TypeScript: Ensure the TypeScript version used for development matches the version specified in tsconfig.json and is compatible with the @types/* packages and actual library versions.
   * Database Drivers: Specific database driver versions must match the PostgreSQL server version used.
3. AI Module (Python)
 * Package Manager: pip with a virtual environment manager (venv or conda).
   * Recommendation: Use pip for installing packages. Crucially, use venv (standard library) or conda (for complex scientific/data environments) to create isolated environments for each Python microservice/ML model. This prevents dependency conflicts between different projects.
 * Configuration Files:
   * requirements.txt: Simple list of direct dependencies (pip freeze > requirements.txt). Less robust than Pipfile.lock.
   * Pipfile and Pipfile.lock (with pipenv): Highly recommended. Pipfile defines direct dependencies, and Pipfile.lock locks down the exact versions of all dependencies (direct and transitive) for deterministic builds, similar to package-lock.json.
   * conda.yml (with conda): For managing environments and dependencies when using Anaconda/Miniconda.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * ML Frameworks: tensorflow or pytorch
   * Data Manipulation: pandas, numpy
   * Scientific Computing: scipy
   * Machine Learning: scikit-learn
   * NLP: nltk, spacy, transformers (Hugging Face)
   * API Serving: fastapi or flask
   * HTTP Client: requests
   * MLOps Libraries: mlflow, boto3 (for AWS S3/SageMaker interaction)
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * Environment Isolation: The primary strategy for Python. Each AI microservice or ML training pipeline gets its own isolated virtual environment.
   * ML Framework Versions: TensorFlow and PyTorch can have strict compatibility requirements with Python versions, CUDA versions (for GPU), and other libraries. Carefully consult their documentation.
   * Dependency Resolution: pipenv is much better at resolving complex dependency trees than bare pip and requirements.txt.
   * Docker: For production, the Python environment and all dependencies will be baked into a Docker image, ensuring perfect reproducibility regardless of the host system.
4. AR/VR Module (Unity 3D - C#)
 * Package Manager:
   * Unity Package Manager (UPM): Manages official Unity packages (e.g., ARFoundation, XR Interaction Toolkit), verified third-party packages, and custom packages.
   * .NET (NuGet): While Unity typically handles most dependencies via UPM, for specific C# libraries outside of the Unity ecosystem, NuGet might be used (less common for core game dev, more for backend-like services within Unity).
 * Configuration Files:
   * Packages/manifest.json: Defines the UPM package dependencies and their versions for the project.
   * Packages/packages-lock.json: Locks specific versions of packages, ensuring deterministic builds.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * AR/VR: ARFoundation, ARCore XR Plugin, ARKit XR Plugin, XR Interaction Toolkit (for VR interactions).
   * Networking: UnityWebRequest (built-in) or a C# HTTP client library.
   * JSON Handling: Newtonsoft.Json (commonly used for API responses).
   * 3D Model Importers/Optimizers: Often built-in or specific assets from the Unity Asset Store.
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * Unity Version: UPM packages are strongly tied to specific Unity editor versions. Upgrading Unity often requires upgrading UPM packages.
   * XR Plugin Compatibility: ARCore/ARKit plugins must be compatible with both the ARFoundation version and the target device OS versions.
   * Asset Store Purchases: Manage third-party assets from the Unity Asset Store. Keep them updated and check for compatibility with your Unity version.
5. Go Modules (Potential for specific microservices/CLI tools)
If any microservices or command-line tools are written in Go (e.g., for performance-critical components or specific network proxies).
 * Package Manager: Go Modules. Built directly into the Go toolchain.
 * Configuration Files:
   * go.mod: Defines the module path, Go version, and direct dependencies (module paths and minimum versions).
   * go.sum: Contains cryptographic checksums of all direct and indirect dependencies, ensuring reproducible builds. This file should always be committed to version control.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * Web Frameworks (if applicable): gin-gonic/gin or gorilla/mux
   * Database Driver: lib/pq (PostgreSQL)
   * JSON Handling: encoding/json (built-in)
   * HTTP Client: net/http (built-in)
   * Kafka Client: segmentio/kafka-go
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * Semantic Import Versioning: Go modules enforce semantic versioning in import paths for major versions (e.g., github.com/foo/bar/v2).
   * go mod tidy: Regularly run this to clean up unused dependencies and add missing ones.
   * Deterministic Builds: go.sum ensures exact dependency versions are used.
Overarching Dependency Management Practices in CI/CD:
 * Automated Dependency Scans: Integrate security scanning tools (e.g., Snyk, Trivy, SonarQube, or built-in npm audit/pip audit in CI) to automatically detect vulnerabilities in dependencies.
 * Linting & Formatting: Enforce consistent code style across all languages using linters (ESLint for JS/TS, Black/Flake8 for Python, Prettier for formatting, Go fmt/vet for Go, StyleCop for C#).
 * Unit & Integration Tests: Ensure comprehensive test suites run on every dependency update to catch breaking changes or regressions.
 * Containerization (Docker): Crucially, Docker will encapsulate each microservice's specific runtime environment and its exact dependencies. The Dockerfile will explicitly list the npm install, pip install, go mod download, etc., commands, ensuring that the deployed image contains precisely the required packages. This minimizes "works on my machine" issues.
 * Base Images: Use hardened and minimal base Docker images (e.g., node:alpine, python:slim-buster, golang:alpine) to reduce attack surface and image size.
 * Dependency Caching: In CI/CD pipelines, cache node_modules, pip caches, and Go module caches to speed up build times.

 * Deployment scripts: Creating robust scripts for installation, deployment, and containerization.
 * Security considerations: Implementing proper authentication, authorization, data encryption, and other security measures.
4. Database Interactions (SQL/TypeORM for Backend, Conceptual for AI)
We've already seen TypeORM in the NestJS examples. Here's a brief look at conceptual SQL and how the AI might interact with data.
Sample SQL for Database Setup (PostgreSQL)
-- Create ENUM types first
CREATE TYPE user_type AS ENUM ('consumer', 'retailer', 'admin', 'moderator');
CREATE TYPE strain_type AS ENUM ('indica', 'sativa', 'hybrid');
CREATE TYPE order_status AS ENUM ('pending', 'confirmed', 'processing', 'shipped', 'delivered', 'cancelled', 'refunded');
CREATE TYPE payment_status AS ENUM ('paid', 'pending', 'failed', 'refunded');
CREATE TYPE delivery_type AS ENUM ('delivery', 'pickup');
CREATE TYPE article_status AS ENUM ('draft', 'published', 'archived');
CREATE TYPE item_type AS ENUM ('strain', 'product', 'article');
CREATE TYPE interaction_type AS ENUM ('view', 'click', 'add_to_cart', 'purchase', 'rate');
CREATE TYPE pod_product_type AS ENUM ('2d_print', '3d_print');


-- users Table
CREATE TABLE users (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    username VARCHAR(50) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    email VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    password_hash VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    full_name VARCHAR(255),
    date_of_birth DATE NOT NULL,
    phone_number VARCHAR(20) UNIQUE,
    profile_picture_url TEXT,
    bio TEXT,
    location_country VARCHAR(100),
    location_state VARCHAR(100),
    user_type user_type NOT NULL DEFAULT 'consumer',
    is_active BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,
    last_login_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- retailers Table
CREATE TABLE retailers (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    user_id BIGINT UNIQUE REFERENCES users(id),
    name VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    license_number VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    address_street VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    address_city VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL,
    address_state VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL,
    address_zip_code VARCHAR(20) NOT NULL,
    address_country VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL,
    latitude NUMERIC(10,7),
    longitude NUMERIC(10,7),
    phone_number VARCHAR(20),
    email VARCHAR(255),
    website_url TEXT,
    operating_hours JSONB,
    logo_url TEXT,
    description TEXT,
    is_verified BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- categories Table
CREATE TABLE categories (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    slug VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    description TEXT,
    parent_id BIGINT REFERENCES categories(id),
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- tags Table
CREATE TABLE tags (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    slug VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    type VARCHAR(50),
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- strains Table
CREATE TABLE strains (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    slug VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    strain_type strain_type NOT NULL,
    description TEXT,
    lineage TEXT,
    thc_min NUMERIC(5,2),
    thc_max NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbd_min NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbd_max NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbn_min NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbn_max NUMERIC(5,2),
    aroma_profile TEXT,
    image_urls TEXT[],
    medical_uses_summary TEXT,
    cultivation_notes TEXT,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- strain_terpenes Table
CREATE TABLE strain_terpenes (
    strain_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES strains(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
    terpene_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES terpenes(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
    percentage NUMERIC(5,2),
    PRIMARY KEY (strain_id, terpene_id)
);

-- terpenes Table
CREATE TABLE terpenes (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    name VARCHAR(100) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    description TEXT,
    aroma VARCHAR(255),
    medical_benefits TEXT,
    image_url TEXT,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- products Table
CREATE TABLE products (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    retailer_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES retailers(id),
    name VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    slug VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    description TEXT,
    category_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES categories(id),
    strain_id BIGINT REFERENCES strains(id),
    brand VARCHAR(100),
    price NUMERIC(10,2) NOT NULL,
    currency VARCHAR(3) NOT NULL DEFAULT 'USD',
    thc_content NUMERIC(5,2),
    cbd_content NUMERIC(5,2),
    unit_of_measure VARCHAR(50),
    quantity_per_unit NUMERIC(10,2),
    inventory_count INTEGER,
    image_urls TEXT[],
    lab_test_url TEXT,
    is_available BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,
    metadata JSONB,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    UNIQUE (retailer_id, slug)
);

-- product_tags Table
CREATE TABLE product_tags (
    product_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES products(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
    tag_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES tags(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
    PRIMARY KEY (product_id, tag_id)
);

-- reviews Table
CREATE TABLE reviews (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    user_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES users(id),
    strain_id BIGINT REFERENCES strains(id),
    product_id BIGINT REFERENCES products(id),
    retailer_id BIGINT REFERENCES retailers(id),
    rating SMALLINT NOT NULL CHECK (rating >= 1 AND rating <= 5),
    title VARCHAR(255),
    comment TEXT,
    effects_felt TEXT[],
    symptoms_helped TEXT[],
    is_verified_purchase BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
    CHECK ( (strain_id IS NOT NULL AND product_id IS NULL AND retailer_id IS NULL) OR
            (product_id IS NOT NULL AND strain_id IS NULL AND retailer_id IS NULL) OR
            (retailer_id IS NOT NULL AND strain_id IS NULL AND product_id IS NULL) )
);

-- recommendation_logs Table (for AI training data)
CREATE TABLE recommendation_logs (
    id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
    user_id BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES users(id),
    recommended_item_id BIGINT NOT NULL,
    item_type item_type NOT NULL,
    recommendation_source VARCHAR(100),
    interaction_type interaction_type NOT NULL,
    rating_given SMALLINT CHECK (rating_given >= 1 AND rating_given <= 5),
    context_data JSONB,
    logged_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);

-- Add indexes where appropriate
CREATE INDEX idx_users_email ON users(email);
CREATE INDEX idx_users_username ON users(username);
CREATE INDEX idx_retailers_name ON retailers(name);
CREATE INDEX idx_strains_name ON strains(name);
CREATE INDEX idx_products_name ON products(name);
