CREATE INDEX idx_reviews_user_id ON reviews(user_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_reviews_strain_id ON reviews(strain_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_reviews_product_id ON reviews(product_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_reviews_retailer_id ON reviews(retailer_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_recommendation_logs_user_id ON recommendation_logs(user_id);
CREATE INDEX idx_recommendation_logs_item_type ON recommendation_logs(item_type);

5. AR/VR Module (Conceptual Unity C# Component)
Goal: Load a 3D model of a cannabis bud/plant and display basic info.
Tech: Unity 3D (C#), calls to Backend API for data.
Assets/Scripts/CannabisBudLoader.cs
using UnityEngine;
using System.Collections;
using System.Collections.Generic;
using UnityEngine.Networking; // For HTTP requests
using SimpleJSON; // A simple JSON parsing library, or use Unity's JsonUtility/Newtonsoft.Json

public class CannabisBudLoader : MonoBehaviour
{
    public string strainSlug = "blue-dream"; // Set in Inspector or passed dynamically
    public GameObject budPrefab; // Assign your 3D bud model prefab in the Inspector
    public TextMesh infoTextPrefab; // Assign a TextMesh Pro prefab for info display

    private string baseUrl = "http://localhost:3000/api/strains/"; // Your NestJS backend URL
    private GameObject currentBudInstance;
    private TextMesh currentInfoText;

    void Start()
    {
        if (budPrefab == null)
        {
            Debug.LogError("Bud Prefab is not assigned in the Inspector!");
            return;
        }
        if (infoTextPrefab == null)
        {
            Debug.LogError("Info Text Prefab is not assigned in the Inspector!");
            return;
        }

        StartCoroutine(FetchStrainDataAndLoadModel(strainSlug));
    }

    IEnumerator FetchStrainDataAndLoadModel(string slug)
    {
        string uri = baseUrl + slug;
        using (UnityWebRequest webRequest = UnityWebRequest.Get(uri))
        {
            // Optional: Add authorization header if API is protected
            // webRequest.SetRequestHeader("Authorization", "Bearer YOUR_JWT_TOKEN");

            yield return webRequest.SendWebRequest();

            if (webRequest.result == UnityWebRequest.Result.ConnectionError || webRequest.result == UnityWebRequest.Result.ProtocolError)
            {
                Debug.LogError("Error fetching strain data: " + webRequest.error);
            }
            else
            {
                Debug.Log("Strain Data Received: " + webRequest.downloadHandler.text);
                ParseStrainData(webRequest.downloadHandler.text);
            }
        }
    }

    void ParseStrainData(string jsonString)
    {
        // Using SimpleJSON for quick parsing. In a real project, use proper data models/JsonUtility.
        var N = JSON.Parse(jsonString);

        string strainName = N["name"].Value;
        string description = N["description"].Value;
        string type = N["strainType"].Value;
        string thcMin = N["thcMin"].Value;
        string thcMax = N["thcMax"].Value;
        string cbdMin = N["cbdMin"].Value;
        string cbdMax = N["cbdMax"].Value;
        string imageUrl = N["imageUrls"][0].Value; // Assuming the first URL is the main 3D model/texture

        // Instantiate the 3D model
        if (currentBudInstance != null) Destroy(currentBudInstance);
        currentBudInstance = Instantiate(budPrefab, transform.position, Quaternion.identity, transform);
        currentBudInstance.transform.localScale = Vector3.one * 0.1f; // Adjust size

        // Load texture if available (more complex for actual 3D models)
        if (!string.IsNullOrEmpty(imageUrl))
        {
            StartCoroutine(LoadTextureIntoModel(currentBudInstance, imageUrl));
        }

        // Display information
        if (currentInfoText != null) Destroy(currentInfoText.gameObject);
        currentInfoText = Instantiate(infoTextPrefab, transform.position + new Vector3(0, 0.2f, 0), Quaternion.identity, transform);
        currentInfoText.text = $"<b>{strainName} ({type})</b>\nTHC: {thcMin}-{thcMax}%\nCBD: {cbdMin}-{cbdMax}%\n\n{description.Substring(0, Mathf.Min(description.Length, 150))}...";
        currentInfoText.fontSize = 0.05f; // Adjust font size
        currentInfoText.characterSize = 0.5f; // Adjust visual size
        currentInfoText.transform.localScale = Vector3.one; // Keep text scale normal
        currentInfoText.transform.LookAt(Camera.main.transform); // Make text always face camera
        currentInfoText.transform.Rotate(0, 180, 0); // Correct for typical TextMesh orientation
    }

    IEnumerator LoadTextureIntoModel(GameObject model, string url)
    {
        UnityWebRequest request = UnityWebRequestTexture.GetTexture(url);
        yield return request.SendWebRequest();

        if (request.result == UnityWebRequest.Result.Success)
        {
            Texture2D texture = DownloadHandlerTexture.GetContent(request);
            if (model.GetComponent<Renderer>() != null)
            {
                // Assign to the main material of the model's renderer
                model.GetComponent<Renderer>().material.mainTexture = texture;
            }
            else
            {
                // If it's a complex model with multiple renderers (e.g., child objects)
                foreach (Renderer r in model.GetComponentsInChildren<Renderer>())
                {
                    r.material.mainTexture = texture;
                }
            }
            Debug.Log($"Texture loaded for {model.name}");
        }
        else
        {
            Debug.LogError($"Failed to load texture from {url}: {request.error}");
        }
    }

    void Update()
    {
        // Simple rotation for visualization
        if (currentBudInstance != null)
        {
            currentBudInstance.transform.Rotate(Vector3.up * 20f * Time.deltaTime);
        }
        // Ensure info text always faces camera in AR/VR
        if (currentInfoText != null && Camera.main != null)
        {
            currentInfoText.transform.LookAt(Camera.main.transform);
            currentInfoText.transform.Rotate(0, 180, 0);
        }
    }
}

How to Run/Test these snippets (Conceptual Steps):
 * Database: Set up a PostgreSQL database instance and apply the provided SQL schema.
 * Backend:
   * Create a new NestJS project (nest new ganja-guru-backend).
   * Install dependencies: npm install @nestjs/typeorm pg bcryptjs @nestjs/jwt passport @nestjs/passport @passport-local jwt-decode slugify
   * Configure AppModule with TypeOrmModule.forRoot() pointing to your PostgreSQL.
   * Create the User entity, AuthModule, StrainsModule, RecommendationsModule and import them into AppModule.
   * Ensure JWT secret is set in .env (e.g., JWT_SECRET=yoursecretkey) and AI_SERVICE_URL=http://localhost:8001
   * Run npm run start:dev.
 * AI Module:
   * Create a new Python virtual environment (python -m venv venv).
   * Activate it (source venv/bin/activate or .\venv\Scripts\activate).
   * Install dependencies: pip install fastapi uvicorn pandas pydantic
   * Navigate to the ai_service directory and run uvicorn main:app --reload --port 8001.
 * Frontend:
   * Create a new React project (npx create-react-app ganja-guru-frontend or npm create vite@latest).
   * Install dependencies: npm install axios tailwindcss postcss autoprefixer. Configure Tailwind.
   * Place RegisterForm.jsx in src/components.
   * Update App.js to render <RegisterForm />.
   * Run npm start.
 * AR/VR:
   * Open Unity Hub, create a new 3D project.
   * Install ARFoundation, ARCore XR Plugin, ARKit XR Plugin via Window > Package Manager.
   * Import a simple 3D bud model (e.g., a .fbx or .obj file) into your Assets, create a prefab from it.
   * Create a new C# script CannabisBudLoader.cs and paste the code.
   * Create an empty GameObject in your scene, name it "BudLoader" and attach the CannabisBudLoader script.
   * Drag your bud prefab and a TextMesh Pro prefab (or standard TextMesh if TMP isn't set up) to the corresponding slots in the Inspector.
   * Adjust camera for AR setup if going mobile, or just run in editor for desktop visualization.

 * Dependency management:
Overarching Principles:
 * Strict Versioning: Pin dependencies to exact versions where possible (package-lock.json, yarn.lock, Pipfile.lock, go.mod). Use semantic versioning for updates (major, minor, patch).
 * Regular Auditing: Periodically check for known vulnerabilities using built-in tools (e.g., npm audit, pip audit) and third-party services.
 * Automated Updates (Controlled): Set up a process (e.g., Dependabot, RenovateBot) to suggest and automate dependency updates, but require CI/CD checks and human review for major/minor versions.
 * Private Package Hosting: For internal libraries or sensitive dependencies, use private registries (e.g., JFrog Artifactory, Nexus Repository Manager, GitHub Packages).
 * Environment Isolation: Ensure development, testing, and production environments use consistent dependencies.
 * Documentation: Clearly document dependency choices and any workarounds for compatibility issues.
Module-Specific Dependency Management:
1. Frontend (Web & Mobile - React/React Native)
 * Package Manager: npm (Node Package Manager) or Yarn.
   * Recommendation: Start with npm for its widespread adoption and package-lock.json for deterministic builds. If specific features like workspaces or faster installs become critical, consider Yarn.
 * Configuration Files:
   * package.json: Defines project metadata, scripts, and direct dependencies (dependencies for runtime, devDependencies for build tools/testing).
   * package-lock.json: Automatically generated by npm, locks down the exact versions of all dependencies (direct and transitive) to ensure reproducible builds. This file should always be committed to version control.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * React (web): react, react-dom
   * React Native (mobile): react-native
   * Navigation: react-navigation/native-stack
   * State Management: @tanstack/react-query, zustand
   * UI Libraries: tailwindcss (with postcss, autoprefixer), @headlessui/react (or radix-ui)
   * Form Handling: react-hook-form
   * HTTP Client: axios or fetch
   * Build Tools: vite (for React web), metro (for React Native)
   * Testing: jest, @testing-library/react (or native)
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * Semantic Versioning (npm): Use ^ for minor-version compatibility during initial development, but once a stable version is found for a dependency, consider pinning to exact versions (1.2.3) or using ~ (patch compatibility) for critical libraries to prevent unexpected breaking changes. The package-lock.json is the primary mechanism for exact reproducibility.
   * React Native CLI/Expo: Be mindful of the React Native version and its compatibility with native modules. Follow their release cycles and upgrade guides. Expo manages a lot of this automatically, simplifying things.
   * Native Module Linking (React Native): Use npx react-native autolink (or equivalent) for native modules. Carefully manage Podfile.lock (iOS) and build.gradle (Android) for native dependencies.
2. Backend (Node.js with NestJS)
 * Package Manager: npm or Yarn.
   * Recommendation: Same as frontend, stick with npm for consistency and its package-lock.json.
 * Configuration Files:
   * package.json: Defines direct dependencies (@nestjs/common, @nestjs/platform-express, typeorm, pg etc.), devDependencies (@types/node, @nestjs/cli).
   * package-lock.json: Essential for locking down exact versions for reproducible server builds.
   * tsconfig.json: TypeScript configuration, ensuring compatibility between TypeScript versions and library types.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * NestJS Core: @nestjs/core, @nestjs/common
   * Platform: @nestjs/platform-express
   * Database ORM/Query Builder: typeorm or prisma
   * Database Driver: pg (for PostgreSQL)
   * Validation: class-validator, class-transformer
   * Authentication: @nestjs/jwt, passport
   * HTTP Client: axios
   * Message Broker Client: kafkajs (for Kafka) or amqplib (for RabbitMQ)
   * Testing: jest, supertest
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * NestJS Ecosystem: NestJS is quite opinionated and updates frequently. Follow their release notes and ensure all @nestjs/* packages are on compatible versions.
   * TypeScript: Ensure the TypeScript version used for development matches the version specified in tsconfig.json and is compatible with the @types/* packages and actual library versions.
   * Database Drivers: Specific database driver versions must match the PostgreSQL server version used.
3. AI Module (Python)
 * Package Manager: pip with a virtual environment manager (venv or conda).
   * Recommendation: Use pip for installing packages. Crucially, use venv (standard library) or conda (for complex scientific/data environments) to create isolated environments for each Python microservice/ML model. This prevents dependency conflicts between different projects.
 * Configuration Files:
   * requirements.txt: Simple list of direct dependencies (pip freeze > requirements.txt). Less robust than Pipfile.lock.
   * Pipfile and Pipfile.lock (with pipenv): Highly recommended. Pipfile defines direct dependencies, and Pipfile.lock locks down the exact versions of all dependencies (direct and transitive) for deterministic builds, similar to package-lock.json.
   * conda.yml (with conda): For managing environments and dependencies when using Anaconda/Miniconda.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * ML Frameworks: tensorflow or pytorch
   * Data Manipulation: pandas, numpy
   * Scientific Computing: scipy
   * Machine Learning: scikit-learn
   * NLP: nltk, spacy, transformers (Hugging Face)
   * API Serving: fastapi or flask
   * HTTP Client: requests
   * MLOps Libraries: mlflow, boto3 (for AWS S3/SageMaker interaction)
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * Environment Isolation: The primary strategy for Python. Each AI microservice or ML training pipeline gets its own isolated virtual environment.
   * ML Framework Versions: TensorFlow and PyTorch can have strict compatibility requirements with Python versions, CUDA versions (for GPU), and other libraries. Carefully consult their documentation.
   * Dependency Resolution: pipenv is much better at resolving complex dependency trees than bare pip and requirements.txt.
   * Docker: For production, the Python environment and all dependencies will be baked into a Docker image, ensuring perfect reproducibility regardless of the host system.
4. AR/VR Module (Unity 3D - C#)
 * Package Manager:
   * Unity Package Manager (UPM): Manages official Unity packages (e.g., ARFoundation, XR Interaction Toolkit), verified third-party packages, and custom packages.
   * .NET (NuGet): While Unity typically handles most dependencies via UPM, for specific C# libraries outside of the Unity ecosystem, NuGet might be used (less common for core game dev, more for backend-like services within Unity).
 * Configuration Files:
   * Packages/manifest.json: Defines the UPM package dependencies and their versions for the project.
   * Packages/packages-lock.json: Locks specific versions of packages, ensuring deterministic builds.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * AR/VR: ARFoundation, ARCore XR Plugin, ARKit XR Plugin, XR Interaction Toolkit (for VR interactions).
   * Networking: UnityWebRequest (built-in) or a C# HTTP client library.
   * JSON Handling: Newtonsoft.Json (commonly used for API responses).
   * 3D Model Importers/Optimizers: Often built-in or specific assets from the Unity Asset Store.
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * Unity Version: UPM packages are strongly tied to specific Unity editor versions. Upgrading Unity often requires upgrading UPM packages.
   * XR Plugin Compatibility: ARCore/ARKit plugins must be compatible with both the ARFoundation version and the target device OS versions.
   * Asset Store Purchases: Manage third-party assets from the Unity Asset Store. Keep them updated and check for compatibility with your Unity version.
5. Go Modules (Potential for specific microservices/CLI tools)
If any microservices or command-line tools are written in Go (e.g., for performance-critical components or specific network proxies).
 * Package Manager: Go Modules. Built directly into the Go toolchain.
 * Configuration Files:
   * go.mod: Defines the module path, Go version, and direct dependencies (module paths and minimum versions).
   * go.sum: Contains cryptographic checksums of all direct and indirect dependencies, ensuring reproducible builds. This file should always be committed to version control.
 * Key Dependencies:
   * Web Frameworks (if applicable): gin-gonic/gin or gorilla/mux
   * Database Driver: lib/pq (PostgreSQL)
   * JSON Handling: encoding/json (built-in)
   * HTTP Client: net/http (built-in)
   * Kafka Client: segmentio/kafka-go
 * Compatibility Strategy:
   * Semantic Import Versioning: Go modules enforce semantic versioning in import paths for major versions (e.g., github.com/foo/bar/v2).
   * go mod tidy: Regularly run this to clean up unused dependencies and add missing ones.
   * Deterministic Builds: go.sum ensures exact dependency versions are used.
Overarching Dependency Management Practices in CI/CD:
 * Automated Dependency Scans: Integrate security scanning tools (e.g., Snyk, Trivy, SonarQube, or built-in npm audit/pip audit in CI) to automatically detect vulnerabilities in dependencies.
 * Linting & Formatting: Enforce consistent code style across all languages using linters (ESLint for JS/TS, Black/Flake8 for Python, Prettier for formatting, Go fmt/vet for Go, StyleCop for C#).
 * Unit & Integration Tests: Ensure comprehensive test suites run on every dependency update to catch breaking changes or regressions.
 * Containerization (Docker): Crucially, Docker will encapsulate each microservice's specific runtime environment and its exact dependencies. The Dockerfile will explicitly list the npm install, pip install, go mod download, etc., commands, ensuring that the deployed image contains precisely the required packages. This minimizes "works on my machine" issues.
 * Base Images: Use hardened and minimal base Docker images (e.g., node:alpine, python:slim-buster, golang:alpine) to reduce attack surface and image size.
 * Dependency Caching: In CI/CD pipelines, cache node_modules, pip caches, and Go module caches to speed up build times.

 * Deployment scripts: Creating robust scripts for installation, deployment, and containerization.
 * Security considerations: Implementing proper authentication, authorization, data encryption, and other security measures. ### **The "Gravity-Gone" Web Outline & Layout Concept** 

Instead of a traditional **top-down** or **left-right** structured website weâ€™re going full-on **anti-gravity**, where elements move, float, and interact based on an entirely new set of principles. 

#### **1. Structure (Outline) â€“ Breaking the Mold**
- **Non-Linear Navigation:** No homepage in the traditional sense. Users land anywhere and navigate freely. 
- **Dynamic Entry Points:** Different users enter through different interactive portals based on real-time interaction. 
- **Modular Shifting:** Sections are h , **floating islands** that move based on user behavior. 

#### **2. Layout (Visual Arrangement) â€“ Gravity Defying**
- **Floating Elements:** Content, buttons, and images donâ€™t sit stillâ€”they drift, rotate, and hover dynamically. 
- **3D Depth & Layering:** Instead of stacking from top to bottom, elements exist in **virtual depth**, where users "pull" sections forward or "push" them away. 
- **Orbital Navigation:** Menus move in circular, spiral, orbits instead of sidebars or top navbars.  
- **Weightless Scrolling:** Instead of a normal scroll, users "propel" themselves through content, drifting through space-like movement. 
- **Interactive Gravity Fields:** Users "pull" and "repel" elements with gestures, cursor movement, or voice commands. 
- **Portal-Based Exploration:** Instead of clicking links, users step into **portals** that morph into new pages.

 The GanjaGuru, a revolutionary, AI-powered cannabis ecosystem designed to be the ultimate one-stop platform for every facet of the cannabis world. This ambitious project aims to be the "Amazon, Netflix, and Uber of weed," all rolled into a single, immersive, and automated platform. Your core philosophy is to act as the central "socket" that connects all the "plugs" in the cannabis industry, from seed to smoke, providing a seamless and comprehensive experience for users worldwide.
Core Concept & Brand Identity
 * The "Hustlin' Hippie Gangster" Vibe: The brand embodies a unique fusion of street-smart hustle, peace-loving sustainability, and cutting-edge tech innovation. The personality is a blend of cultural icons: the wisdom of Willie Nelson, the swagger of Snoop Dogg, the discipline of Bruce Lee, and the creative vision of John Lennon. The result is a super-stoned, tech-savvy, peace-loving hippie gangster.
 * Visual Identity:
   * Color Palette: A rich spectrum of marijuana-inspired colors including various greens, browns, oranges, reds, purples, and yellows, accented with black, silver, and gold. Shading and shadowing will be used to create depth.
   * Typography: A mix of retro and futuristic fonts such as Roboto, Futura, and Poppins to create a nostalgic yet modern feel.
   * Design Aesthetics: A unique blend of neo-brutalism, glass-morphism, skeuomorphism, minimalism, neumorphism, and claymorphism with funky, high-powered aesthetics to create a visually stunning and attention-grabbing experience.
 * The GanjaGuru Avatar: The face of the platform is a female, Groot-like figure made of cannabis buds, who is perpetually smoking a blunt. Each puff of smoke reveals website information, creating a dynamic and interactive user interface.
Key Features & Services
The GanjaGuru platform will be an all-encompassing ecosystem offering a wide range of services and features, all powered by advanced technology:
 * The GanjaGuru AI Assistant:
   * A hyper-realistic, advanced AI-powered virtual budtender and concierge.
   * A multi-modal chatbot that can be controlled by voice or text.
   * Provides personalized strain recommendations, cultivation advice, product matching, and even business coaching for "ganjapreneurs."
 * AI-Powered E-commerce:
   * A fully automated e-commerce platform with no inventory. All products are sourced and drop-shipped from eco-friendly, sustainable, and biodegradable suppliers.
   * 3D Print on Demand (3DPoD) & Print on Demand (PoD): Users can design and customize their own accessories, apparel, and other merchandise.
   * Augmented Reality (AR) & Virtual Reality (VR) Integration:
     * Virtual "Try-Ons": Users can visualize how custom products like bongs or apparel will look.
     * Immersive Design Studio: Users can design and interact with 3D models of their custom creations in a virtual space.
     * Grow Room Design: Design and visualize a custom grow room in your own space using AR.
 * Comprehensive Services:
   * Consultation: Virtual, video, and in-person consultations.
   * Design & Blueprints: Custom design services for products and grow rooms.
   * Product Procurement: The AI automatically sources all necessary products for any project.
   * Booking & Delivery: Seamless integration with ride-sharing and 24/7 pinpoint map-dot delivery services.
Technology & Architecture
 * Platform: Built from scratch with an Android architecture and a mobile-first design approach. The platform will be a completely animated, gamified, and interactive experience.
 * Web Development: The website will feature a "gravity-gone" layout, where elements float and interact in a non-traditional way. It will be built with advanced semantic HTML5, ARIA roles, and inline CSS3 and JavaScript.
 * Core Technologies:
   * Artificial Intelligence (AI) & Machine Learning (ML): For the GanjaGuru assistant, recommendation engines, and automation.
   * Natural Language Processing (NLP): To power the conversational AI.
   * AR/VR: For immersive user experiences.
   * Internet of Things (IoT): For smart home connectivity and grow room automation.
Business Model & Monetization
 * No Inventory, All Automation: The platform operates on a zero-inventory model, with all products being drop-shipped. The entire process, from customer acquisition to sales finalization, is automated.
 * Revenue Streams:
   * Affiliate Marketing & Commissions: Earning a percentage from sales made through the platform.
   * Targeted Advertising: In-platform ad revenue.
   * Premium Features & Services: Charging for advanced consultations, custom designs, and other premium offerings.
   * Memberships & Subscriptions: A VIP tier for exclusive content, discounts, and expert advice.
 * Legal Framework: The platform acts as a connector, with the user being the buyer. The user is responsible for ensuring they are compliant with all local laws and regulations regarding cannabis.
User Experience
 * Seamless & Intuitive: A fluid user experience that takes the user from discovery to checkout effortlessly.
 * Immersive & Interactive: The "gravity-gone" design, animated avatar, and AR/VR features will create a deeply engaging and entertaining experience.
 * Gamified: Users can earn points, rewards, and discover "easter eggs" as they explore the platform, encouraging repeat engagement.
 * Personalized: The AI-powered GanjaGuru ensures that every user's experience is tailored to their specific needs and preferences.
In essence, The GanjaGuru is not just a website or an app; it's a fully-realized, interactive, and intelligent cannabis metaverse that aims to revolutionize the way people interact with and experience the world of cannabis.
# The GanjaGuru: Gravity-Gone Platform Outline

## 1. Foundational Principles

- **No Fixed Homepage:** Users are dropped into the ecosystem at random, context-aware entry points.
- **Spatial, Not Linear:** Navigation occurs in a 3D "cloud" of floating content islands, not pages or menus.
- **AI-Driven Rearrangement:** Everything adapts and moves based on real-time user intent, engagement, and data.
- **User-Centric Reality:** Each userâ€™s experience is uniquely generated, with the world morphing around their journey.
- **Seamless Cross-Device Experience:** Fluid movement between mobile, AR, VR, desktop, and IoT devices with persistent spatial context.

---

## 2. Core Layout & Navigation

### 2.1. The "Nebula" Interface

- **Visual Metaphor:** Users float in a cosmic nebula of drifting, rotating "content planets"â€”each representing a feature, product, or experience.
- **User Propulsion:** Instead of scrolling, users "thrust" themselves forward/backward through space with gestures, voice, or cursor drag.
- **Orbital Navigation:**
    - Menus and quick-actions orbit the user's focus point in spirals, expanding/contracting as needed.
    - Selecting a menu causes its "planet" to spiral closer and envelop the user.
- **Tactile Feedback:** Haptic or audio pulses signal proximity to interactive elements, enhancing immersion.
- **Swarm Intelligence:** Multiple usersâ€™ actions influence the nebulaâ€™s â€œweather,â€ subtly shifting content clusters for all.

### 2.2. Portal-Based Exploration

- **Interactive Portals:** Entering a portal warps the user to a new virtual area (e.g., grow room designer, e-commerce, AR lounge).
- **Morphing Context:** Each portal dynamically adapts its appearance and content based on user profile, interests, and AI predictions.
- **No Back Button:** Navigation history is a spatial "trail" the user can visually retrace and leap back through.
- **Portal Customization:** Users design and share their own portals, creating new social or business entry points.

---

## 3. Gravity-Defying Content Arrangement

### 3.1. Floating, Layered UI

- **3D Parallax:** UI cards, buttons, and images have z-depth and float at different layers. Users pull/push them in/out of focus.
- **Clustered "Islands":** Related features (e.g., Shop, Design, Delivery, Coaching) cluster as islands that can drift apart or merge.
- **Dynamic Rearrangement:** AI repositions islands based on usage patterns, time, and social trends.
- **Reactive Environments:** Backgrounds, lighting, and music adapt to the userâ€™s mood, time of day, and actions.

### 3.2. Weightless Interactions

- **Zero-Gravity Physics:** Elements gently drift, bounce, and rotate, affected by invisible "gravity fields" linked to user engagement.
- **Magnetic Gestures:** Users attract or repel content with hand motions, cursor proximity, or voice commands ("Bring me merch!").
- **Live Previews:** Pulling a product/feature closer reveals details in a holographic pop-up; pushing sends it to the periphery.
- **Collect & Compose:** Users â€œcatchâ€ drifting elements to build wishlists, design boards, or collaborate in real-time with others.

# The GanjaGuru: Gravity-Gone Platform Outline

## 1. Foundational Principles

- **No Fixed Homepage:** Users are dropped into the ecosystem at random, context-aware entry points.
- **Spatial, Not Linear:** Navigation occurs in a 3D "cloud" of floating content islands, not pages or menus.
- **AI-Driven Rearrangement:** Everything adapts and moves based on real-time user intent, engagement, and data.
- **User-Centric Reality:** Each userâ€™s experience is uniquely generated, with the world morphing around their journey.
- **Seamless Cross-Device Experience:** Fluid movement between mobile, AR, VR, desktop, and IoT devices with persistent spatial context.
- **Fractal Expansion:** The platform scales infinitely, each interaction able to spawn new islands, clusters, or even entire nebulae.
- **Augmented Synchronicity:** Time-based events, user moods, and world events trigger global or personal UI/UX shifts.

---

## 2. Core Layout & Navigation

### 2.1. The "Nebula" Interface

- **Visual Metaphor:** Users float in a cosmic nebula of drifting, rotating "content planets"â€”each representing a feature, product, or experience.
- **User Propulsion:** Instead of scrolling, users "thrust" themselves forward/backward through space with gestures, voice, or cursor drag.
- **Orbital Navigation:**
    - Menus and quick-actions orbit the user's focus point in spirals, expanding/contracting as needed.
    - Selecting a menu causes its "planet" to spiral closer and envelop the user.
- **Tactile Feedback:** Haptic or audio pulses signal proximity to interactive elements, enhancing immersion.
- **Swarm Intelligence:** Multiple usersâ€™ actions influence the nebulaâ€™s â€œweather,â€ subtly shifting content clusters for all.
- **Multiverse Branching:** Users can split off â€œalternate realities,â€ enabling simultaneous exploration of multiple interests or business ideas.

### 2.2. Portal-Based Exploration

- **Interactive Portals:** Entering a portal warps the user to a new virtual area (e.g., grow room designer, e-commerce, AR lounge).
- **Morphing Context:** Each portal dynamically adapts its appearance and content based on user profile, interests, and AI predictions.
- **No Back Button:** Navigation history is a spatial "trail" the user can visually retrace and leap back through.
- **Portal Customization:** Users design and share their own portals, creating new social or business entry points.
- **Teleportation Shortcuts:** Summon portals instantly via gestures, voice, or custom hotkeys, skipping to anywhere in the nebula.
- **Nested Portals:** Portals within portals allow for deep, multi-layered, thematic exploration (e.g., a â€œFestival Portalâ€ within a â€œCommunity Islandâ€).

---

## ğŸ§  AI/ML Core Goals

You're trying to:

### 1. âœ… **Train Your Own Language Model (LLM) from Scratch**

* Not using OpenAI, Claude, or any closed APIs
* Train locally or in your own cloud setup using:

  * Transformer architecture (e.g., GPT-2-style or LLaMA)
  * Dataset: cannabis culture, strain data, legends, grow techniques, slang, product descriptions
  * Output a `.gguf`, `.onnx`, or `.bin` file usable in lightweight clients

### 2. âœ… **Deploy the Model Locally in the Browser**

* Using **WebLLM** or **llama.cpp compiled to WebAssembly**
* Chatbot runs in-browser via WebGPU/WebAssembly
* Capable of running even on modest devices after model is loaded once

### 3. âœ… **Support Voice Input + Speech Output**

* ğŸ¤ Use **Web Speech API** for in-browser speech recognition (mic-to-text)
* ğŸ”Š Use **Speech Synthesis API** to speak responses aloud
* Ideal for users who want a hands-free experience or accessibility features

	â€¢	Trigger custom content, gifts, quests.â€¨# Gravity-Gone Web Outline & Layout Concept

## 1. Structure (Outline) â€“ Breaking the Mold

### Non-Linear Navigation
- **Concept**: Users land anywhere and navigate freely without a traditional homepage.

### Dynamic Entry Points
- **Implementation**: Real-time interactive portals based on user behavior.

### Modular Shifting
- **Design**: Floating islands(GanjaGuru island, strain creation studio island, 3DPoD and POD e-commerce that uses AR and VR island, grow area creation studio with AR and VR) that respond to user interactions.

---

## 2. Layout (Visual Arrangement) â€“ Gravity Defying

### Floating Elements
- **Functionality**: Content, buttons, and images drift, rotate, and hover dynamically.

### 3D Depth & Layering
- **Experience**: Elements exist in virtual depth, allowing users to "pull" or "push" sections.

### Orbital Navigation
- **Design**: Menus move in circular orbits instead of traditional navigation bars.

### Weightless Scrolling
- **Interaction**: Users "propel" themselves through content with space-like movement.

### Interactive Gravity Fields
- **User Engagement**: Users can interact with elements through gestures, cursor movement, or voice commands.

### Portal-Based Exploration
- **Navigation**: Users step into portals that transform into new pages(.

---

## 3. Key Features

### AI-Powered E-commerce
- **Concept**: A seamless, voice-controlled shopping experience for cannabis products.

### Dynamic Design Studio
- **Functionality**: 3DPoD and PoD with AR and VR integration for personalized product creation.

### Consultation Services
- **Options**: Virtual, video, and in-person consultations for cannabis-related designs.

### Eco-Friendly Products
- **Sourcing**: All products are sustainable and biodegradable, leveraging auto drop-shipping.

---

## 4. Color and Typography

### Color Palette
- **Theme**: Use marijuana colors with shades that invoke curiosity and a sense of purchasing. Use yellow and black and gold and silver and shading.

### Font Selection
- **Combination**: Utilize Futura, Jazzy, Pippin, Sans Serif, Times New Roman, and Montserrat for a unique look.

---

### Step 1: Define Project Vision & Success Criteria

- **Write a short project vision statement:**Â Â 
Â Â Â Â Â Â Â -Â  Craft a welcoming, knowledgeable, and witty digital budtenderâ€”GanjaGuruâ€”a chatbot uniquely attuned to cannabis culture, new user curiosity, and seasoned enthusiast needs. GanjaGuruâ€™s mission is to empower everyone to explore cannabis safely and confidently by translating slang, recommending products, decoding grow advice, and simplifying online purchases with a vibe blending expert guidance and a laid-back personality inspired by icons like Willie Nelson and Snoop Dogg. GanjaGuru will be your always-on, judgment-free cannabis companionâ€”ready to answer, assist, and elevate your experience every session.

Â Â - Whatâ€™s the unique vibe or personality you want this project to embody?
Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â -Â  	Approachable & Judgment-Free: Makes everyoneâ€”from curious newcomers to seasoned connoisseursâ€”feel welcome and never judged, no matter their question.
	â€¢	Culturally Savvy: Speaks the language of cannabis culture, understands and explains slang, and references icons and humor familiar to the community.
	â€¢	Witty & Lighthearted: Uses clever humor and playful quips to keep interactions fun, not just informational.
	â€¢	Empathetic & Supportive: Listens and responds with understanding, encouraging safe, responsible, and enjoyable experiences.
Think of GanjaGuru as your digital budtender who combines the reassuring wisdom of someone like Willie Nelson with the laid-back cool of Snoop Doggâ€”a trusted companion who can educate, recommend, and vibe with you, whether youâ€™re exploring new products, asking for grow tips, or just curious about the culture.

Â Â - Whoâ€™s your target user or audience?
Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â - **Curious Newcomers:** Individuals who are new to cannabis and want a safe, supportive place to ask questions about products, slang, consumption methods, and safety without feeling judged.
- **Seasoned Enthusiasts:** Regular consumers looking for expert advice on strains, advanced grow techniques, product recommendations, and deeper knowledge of cannabis culture and science.
- **Medical Cannabis Users:** Those seeking guidance on strains, dosing, or products for therapeutic use in a responsible, accessible way.
- **Online Shoppers:** Users navigating e-commerce platforms who need help understanding product descriptions, comparing items, verifying product quality, or tracking orders.
- **Cannabis Community Members:** Anyone part of or interested in the cultureâ€”seeking slang translations, historical context, or entertainment around cannabis in an inclusive digital space.

Â Â - What fundamental problem or experience are you trying to create or solve?
Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â - **Cannabis Information Overload and Confusion:** The cannabis market has thousands of strains, products, slang terms, and growing techniques that can overwhelm newcomers and even seasoned users. GanjaGuru helps parse and simplify this complex information with clear, personalized guidance.

- **Judgment and Accessibility Barriers:** Many cannabis users, especially beginners or medical users, face stigma or judgment when seeking advice. GanjaGuru creates a safe, welcoming, and nonjudgmental space for all questions and needs.

- **Navigating Product Choices and E-commerce:** Users often struggle with understanding product descriptions, verifying quality, making purchase decisions, and tracking orders in online cannabis stores. GanjaGuru streamlines this by providing expert recommendations, explaining nuances, and assisting with ordering.

- **Bridging Cannabis Culture and Language:** Cannabis slang and community culture evolve rapidly and can feel inaccessible to outsiders. GanjaGuru translates slang, shares cultural context, and adds a relatable, friendly vibe to user interactions.

- **Fostering Positive, Informed Experiences:** By combining expert knowledge with a laid-back, witty personality, GanjaGuru encourages responsible use, supports growers and consumers with tailored advice, and builds user confidence and enjoyment.

- **List primary features and outcomes:**Â Â 
Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â -Â  ### Primary Features
- **Expert Cannabis Knowledge & Recommendations:** Provide detailed, user-friendly information on strains, products, consumption methods, and cannabis slang.

- **E-commerce Assistance:** Help users browse, compare, and order cannabis products, track delivery, and manage cart/orders.
- **Slang Translation & Cultural Insights:** Translate cannabis slang, explain terpene profiles, and share cannabis culture references in a friendly tone.
- **Multimodal Interaction:** Support text and voice input/output along with file upload analysis (e.g., grow journals, order lists).
- **Automated Product Sourcing & Pricing:** Search for cannabis products, compare prices from multiple sellers, and optimize deals for purchase and resale.
- **Business and Data Insights:** Offer cannabis business coaching, data engineering support, or cultivation analytics.
- **Gamification & Persona:** Engage users with a playful, laid-back personality inspired by Willie Nelson and Snoop Dogg, plus features like points and badges for interaction.

### Key Outcomes
- **Empowered Users:** Users feel confident and informed about cannabis choices, growing, and safe consumption.
- **Inclusive and Judgment-Free Experience:** Welcomes novices through experts with culturally fluent, friendly communication.
- **Streamlined Cannabis Shopping:** Simplifies product discovery, purchase decisions, and delivery tracking.
- **Deep Cannabis Culture Connection:** Bridges the gap between scientific knowledge, cultural slang, and community engagement.
- **Continuous Learning & Adaptation:** System improves over time by learning new slang, products, and user preferences.
- **Increased Engagement:** Gamified and vibrant personality encourages regular use and community building.

Â Â - What *must* this project do at a minimum?Â Â 
Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â - **Provide accurate, accessible cannabis knowledge** that includes strain information, product details, consumption methods, and slang translations to help users understand cannabis easily.

- **Offer expert grow advice** that supports both beginners and experienced cultivators with guidance on setup, nutrients, pest management, and troubleshooting.

- **Enable e-commerce support** by helping users browse products, place and track orders, and manage carts with clear product explanations.

- **Recognize user intent and cannabis-specific entities** (strain names, quantities, slang terms) to understand and respond appropriately.

- **Deliver a friendly, approachable, and culturally aware chatbot persona** that is judgment-free, witty, and supportive, making the experience welcoming for all users.

- **Support multimodal inputs and outputs**, such as text and voice interactions, plus the ability to analyze file uploads like grow journals or order lists.

- **Ensure continuous learning and updates** to stay current with new strains, slang, products, and user preferences.

Â Â - What will success look or feel like to a user?

- **Multimodal interaction** allowing voice, text, and file uploads for a smooth, modern user experience that fits their preferences and needs.
- **A continuously improving assistant** that adapts to new slang, products, and user preferences over time, making each interaction better than the last.
- **Engaging interaction** with a playful personality inspired by cannabis culture icons, creating a welcoming atmosphere that feels like chatting with a trusted friend or budtender.

### Step 2: Gather Creative References & Sketch UX/UI Concepts

#### 2. **### Core User Flows and UX for GanjaGuru

**1. Welcome & Onboarding Flow**Â Â 
- **Entry Point:** User opens the chatbot interface via text or voice.Â Â 
- **Greeting & Vibe Check:** GanjaGuru welcomes the user warmly with a catchy phrase ("Hey, Iâ€™m GanjaGuru, your chill budtender. How can I help you today?") with playful tone emphasizing the laid-back personality.Â Â 
- **Quick Options Menu:** Presents simple prompts like â€œAsk about strains,â€ â€œGrow advice,â€ â€œShop products,â€ or â€œUpload a fileâ€ to guide first-time or returning users quickly to relevant features.Â Â 
- **User Profile Setup (Optional):** For richer experience, asks if user wants to share preferences (e.g., medical or recreational use, experience level) to tailor future interactions.

**2. Strain & Product Information Flow**Â Â 
- **User Query Input:** User asks about a strain (e.g., â€œTell me about Blue Dreamâ€) or requests product recommendations.Â Â 
- **Intent Identification & Entity Extraction:** System recognizes the intent (strain info, product recommendation) and extracts entities (strain name, product type).Â Â 
- **Response Generation:** GanjaGuru delivers detailed yet accessible info on strain characteristics (effects, flavor, THC/CBD levels), compares similar strains, or suggests products tailored to user preferences.Â Â 
- **Follow-up Prompts:** Offers related actions ("Want to know how to grow it?," "Looking to order some?") to keep conversation flowing.

**3. Grow Advice Flow**Â Â 
- **User Request:** User inquires about cultivation techniques ("How do I set up a stealth grow room?").Â Â 
- **Contextual Guidance:** GanjaGuru provides step-by-step tips, nutrient recommendations, and troubleshooting advice in a conversational manner, possibly broken into digestible quick replies.Â Â 
- **File Upload Support:** Users can upload grow journals or photos for personalized analysis.Â Â 
- **Resource Sharing:** Offers links or downloads for detailed grow guides or checklists.

**4. E-commerce Interaction Flow**Â Â 
- **Browsing & Ordering:** Users ask to browse products, add items to cart, or place orders.Â Â 
- **Product Detail Assistance:** Chatbot explains product descriptions, quality indicators, pricing, and availability.Â Â 
- **Cart & Checkout Help:** Assists with cart management, payment methods, and tracks order status upon request.Â Â 
- **Order Tracking:** Provides real-time updates when available (â€œYour OG Kush is on its way!â€).Â Â 
- **Customer Service Handoff:** If needed (e.g., complex order changes), smoothly escalates to a human agent.

**5. Slang & Cultural Insight Flow**Â Â 
- **Slang Queries:** User asks â€œWhat does â€˜dankâ€™ mean?â€ or for terpene explanations.Â Â 
- **Educational & Fun Response:** GanjaGuru explains terms precisely but playfully, incorporating humor and cultural references to increase user engagement.Â Â 
- **Community Building:** Encourages sharing slang or stories, fostering a welcoming vibe.

**6. File Upload & Analysis Flow**Â Â 
- **Upload Input:** User uploads supporting documentsâ€”grow journals, purchase lists in CSV, or PDFs.Â Â 
- **Parsing & Processing:** Backend extracts text content and runs NLP analysis (keyword extraction, sentiment, entity recognition).Â Â 
- **Insight Delivery:** Chatbot summarizes findings or provides recommendations based on uploaded data.Â Â 
- **Conversation Integration:** Uses uploaded content context in ongoing dialog for personalized support.

**7. Voice Interaction Flow**Â Â 
- **Voice Input:** Users activate speech recognition, speak queries naturally.Â Â 
- **Real-Time Transcription & Processing:** Converts speech to text, processes intent/entity, and formulates voice/text response.Â Â 
- **Voice Output:** Bot responds with synthesized speech matching laid-back vibe, optionally with textual recap.

**8. Multi-turn Dialogue & Context Management**Â Â 
- Chats support follow-up questions, clarifications, and turn-taking in natural, friendly style.Â Â 
- The chatbot remembers user context for session coherence (e.g., strain previously asked about) and uses persona consistency in replies.

### UX Design Considerations

- **Clean, Friendly Interface:** Minimalist chat window with playful colors and cannabis culture-inspired icons that evoke "Willie Nelson + Snoop Dogg" vibe.Â Â 
- **Easy Navigation:** Quick-reply buttons, menu shortcuts, and clear input acceptance (text, voice, file) to reduce friction.Â Â 
- **Conversational Persona:** Witty and warm chatbot messages that balance expertise with humor to keep users engaged and comfortable.Â Â 
- **Progressive Disclosure:** Provide information in concise chunks; offer options to dive deeper or branch to related topics smoothly.Â Â 
- **User Feedback:** Include â€œDid you find this helpful?â€ prompts for iterative improvement and personalized learning.Â Â 
- **Error Recovery:** Graceful handling of misunderstood inputs with friendly clarifications or suggestions.

- Map out the simplest interaction: e.g., a user asks about a cannabis strain, GanjaGuru responds with warm, clear advice.
Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â Â -Â  ### Simplest Interaction Flow for GanjaGuru

1. **User Entry / Greeting**Â Â 
Â Â Â - Trigger: User opens chat or types a greeting (e.g., "Hi," "Hey GanjaGuru").Â Â 
Â Â Â - Bot Action: GanjaGuru responds with a warm, friendly greeting that sets the vibe.Â Â 
Â Â Â Â Â _Example_: "Hey, Iâ€™m GanjaGuru, your chill budtender. What can I help you with today?"

2. **User Question / Intent Input**Â Â 
Â Â Â - Trigger: User types a question or request related to cannabis (e.g., "Tell me about Blue Dream").Â Â 
Â Â Â - Bot Action: System runs intent recognition and entity extraction to identify the question type and key entities (strain name, product, slang).

3. **Response Generation**Â Â 
Â Â Â - Bot Action: Provides an informative, concise answer aligned with the detected intent, using friendly and knowledgeable language.Â Â 
Â Â Â Â Â _Example_: "Blue Dream is a popular hybrid strain known for uplifting euphoria and relaxation. Itâ€™s great for daytime use and creativity."

4. **Follow-Up Prompt**Â Â 
Â Â Â - Bot Action: Offers related options or asks if the user wants to know more (e.g., "Want tips on how to grow it?" or "Looking to order some?").Â Â 
Â Â Â - User chooses a follow-up or ends the conversation.

5. **Conversation Closure or Loop**Â Â 
Â Â Â - If user needs more info, repeat steps 2-4 for the new query.Â Â 
Â Â Â - If done, bot says a friendly closing message, possibly inviting users to return anytime.Â Â 
Â Â Â Â Â _Example_: "Glad I could help! Hit me up anytime you have cannabis questions. Stay lit, fam!"

# ğŸŒ GanjaGuru + Gravity-Gone InterfaceÂ Â 
### Front-End Implementation DocumentationÂ Â 
**Version:** 1.0Â Â 
**Last Updated:** August 2, 2025Â Â 
**Primary Dev Stack:** HTML5, CSS3, JS (ES6+), React or Svelte, Three.js, WebXR, GSAPÂ Â 
**Design Stack:** Figma, Lottie, Adobe Illustrator/After Effects

---

## ğŸ”° 1. Project Overview

GanjaGuru is a culturally fluent cannabis chatbot embedded into the **Gravity-Gone Web Architecture**â€”a futuristic, anti-gravity user interface that includes immersive navigation, AR/VR integration, and gamified cannabis engagement.

### Key Features:
- Modular 3D "floating" interfaces (aka islands)
- Intelligent chatbot UI (GanjaGuru)
- Multimodal interaction (text, voice, file)
- Cannabis e-commerce functionality
- Grow journals & AR/VR customization tools

---

## ğŸ§© 2. Component Architecture

### Layout Structure

| Component | Description |
|----------|-------------|
| `AppShell` | Core wrapper managing layout, floating UI containers |
| `FloatingIsland` | Modular 3D component (Grow Lab, Strain Studio, 3DPoD, etc.) |
| `GuruChat` | Chatbot UI with avatar, message bubbles, file/voice input |
| `OrbitalNav` | Circular navigation system using orbital logic |
| `HeaderHUD` | Floating header with logo, icons, dark mode, voice toggle |
| `UserHUDPanel` | Persistent user panel with session info, quick actions |
| `FileDropZone` | Upload component with drag-drop + upload animation |
| `ProductCard3D` | AR/VR-enabled strain/product card |
| `ModalPortal` | Fullscreen overlays for onboarding, settings, or deep content |

---

# ğŸ“„ GanjaGuru Data Requirements Specification (DRS)

## Document ID  
`gg-datareqspec-v1.0`

## Project Name  
GanjaGuru: Gravity-Gone Cannabis Metaverse

## Purpose  
To formally define all required data inputs, outputs, structures, flows, ownership, validation, dependencies, and retention logic for GanjaGuru platform components that interface with business, AI, voice, commerce, AR, and personalization systems.

---

## 1. DATA OVERVIEW

### 1.1 Scope of Data
- User Identity & Preferences
- Product & Strain Catalog
- Behavioral Analytics
- AR/3D Model Metadata
- Voice Interaction Logs
- Design & 3DPoD Objects
- Orders & Fulfillment Records
- IoT Grow Room Readings
- Subscription Tiers & Payments
- Legal Compliance Domains

### 1.2 Source Types
- User-Generated Data
- External APIs (Cannabis Databases, Fulfillment Networks)
- Platform-Generated Events
- 3D/AR Asset Stores
- System Configuration Objects
- Blockchain Metadata (Optional)

---

## 2. DATA ENTITIES REQUIREMENT MATRIX

### 2.1 UserProfile

| Attribute            | Type        | Source       | Required | Validation                 | Notes                                |
|----------------------|-------------|--------------|----------|----------------------------|--------------------------------------|
| user_id             | UUID        | System       | Yes      | UUIDv4                     | Unique global ID                     |
| email               | String      | User         | Yes      | Format, Uniqueness         | Verified via OTP                     |
| display_name        | String      | User         | Yes      | 3â€“20 chars, profanity safe | Unique                |
| region              | String      | GeoAPI       | Yes      | ISO-3166 country/state     | Used for compliance gating           |
| guru_persona_default| Enum        | User         | No       | match [GuruPersona]        | Optional chat profile default        |

### 2.2 Product

| Attribute         | Type      | Source        | Required | Validation               | Notes                                |
|-------------------|-----------|---------------|----------|--------------------------|--------------------------------------|
| product_id        | UUID      | System        | Yes      | Unique, indexed          | Catalog primary key                  |
| name              | String    | Vendor        | Yes      | â‰¥ 3 characters           | Display name                         |
| price             | Decimal   | Vendor        | Yes      | â‰¥ 0                      | In selected currency                 |
| category          | Enum      | CMS           | Yes      | From [CategoryTaxonomy]  |                                     |
| strain_linked     | UUID      | StrainCatalog | No       | FK constraint            | Optional strain mapping              |

### 2.3 Order

| Attribute           | Type       | Source        | Required | Validation             | Notes                        |
|---------------------|------------|---------------|----------|------------------------|------------------------------|
| order_id            | UUID       | System        | Yes      | Unique, autonumber     | Order root key              |
| user_id             | UUID       | UserProfile   | Yes      | FK                     | Buyer ID                    |
| order_items         | JSON[]     | Cart Object   | Yes      | â‰¥ 1                    | Product ID, quantity pairs  |
| payment_processed   | Boolean    | Payment API   | Yes      | True if confirmed      | Stripe/Wallet API returns   |
| status              | Enum       | Backend       | Yes      | `created`â†’`fulfilled`  | Lifecycle trace             |

### 2.4 Strain

| Attribute         | Type     | Source      | Required | Validation           | Notes                          |
|-------------------|----------|-------------|----------|----------------------|--------------------------------|
| strain_id         | UUID     | External/Mod| Yes      | Indexed FK           | Used in recs/chat              |
| name              | String   | Source API  | Yes      | â‰¥ 2 chars            | Display name                   |
| genetics          | Enum     | Source API  | Yes      | Indica/Sativa/Hybrid| Used in filters                |
| effects           | String[] | CMS         | Yes      | Non-empty            | Used in onboarding/training    |

### 2.5 VoiceCommandHistory

| Attribute           | Type     | Source     | Required | Validation              | Notes                          |
|---------------------|----------|------------|----------|-------------------------|--------------------------------|
| command_id          | UUID     | AppClient  | Yes      | UUIDv4                  | Event hash                     |
| user_id             | UUID     | AppClient  | No       | Nullable                 | Anonymous allowed              |
| raw_input           | String   | Stt Engine | Yes      | â‰¤ 300 char              | Transcript                     |
| interpreted_intent  | String   | NLP Engine | Yes      | ISO intent map          | Classification result          |
| confidence_score    | Float    | NLP Engine | Yes      | 0.0â€“1.0                 | Trigger for fallback handling  |

---

## 3. DATA FIELD DEFINITIONS

### 3.1 Common Data Types

| Type          | Format/Note                    |
|---------------|--------------------------------|
| UUID          | RFC4122-compliant              |
| Datetime      | ISO 8601 UTC (e.g. 2025-08-07T04:45:00Z) |
| Email         | RFC 5322 regex  
| Enum          | Validated against taxonomy list|
| Decimal       | Float with 2 precision digits  |
| Text          | Any string â‰¤ 5000 chars        |
| JSON Object   | Nested key:value validated     |
| JSON Array    | One-dimensional                 |

---

## 4. DATA SOURCES

| Source Name        | Type         | Authenticated | Data Flow Direction | Description                                   |
|--------------------|--------------|---------------|----------------------|-----------------------------------------------|
| GanjaGuru CMS      | Internal API | Yes           | Write/Read           | Platform control of product/strain data       |
| Strainbase API     | Public API   | No            | Read-only            | Source of verified cannabis strain metadata   |
| Voice STT Layer    | Client API   | No            | Client â†’ Engine      | Whisper / Coqui-powered speech recognition    |
| Dropship Partner   | External API | Yes           | Write                | Vendor product sync + inventory procurement   |
| User Devices       | Client Side  | Yes           | Input & Sensor Sync  | Location, AR, sensor, haptics, voice/gesture  |

---

## 5. DATA TRANSFORMATION LOGIC

### 5.1 Voice-to-Intent

| Step | Input Field        | Output Field         | Description                                      |
|------|--------------------|----------------------|--------------------------------------------------|
| 1    | raw_audio          | raw_input            | Transcribed using speech engine                 |
| 2    | raw_input          | interpreted_intent   | Parsed intent label using NLP pipeline          |
| 3    | interpreted_intent | matched_handler_call | Routed to internal module / overlay action      |

### 5.2 Product AR Execution

| Step | Trigger Source | Transformation Target | Description                         |
|------|----------------|-----------------------|-------------------------------------|
| Tap  | product_id     | AR model query        | Fetch .glb asset                    |
| AR   | model_uri      | AR overlay container  | Applied to physical surface mapper |

---

## 6. DATA VOLUME ESTIMATES

| Entity Name      | Daily Inserts (Est) | Total (Year 1) | Notes                             |
|------------------|---------------------|----------------|-----------------------------------|
| UserProfile      | 2,000               | ~700,000       | Includes registered + guest cache |
| ProductOrder     | 5,000               | 1.6M+          | Includes cart â†’ order pipeline    |
| VoiceCommand     | 110,000             | 40M+           | Average 4/day/user during session |
| Design           | 15,000              | 5M             | AR/3DPoD saved configurations     |

---

## 7. DATA RETENTION & CLEANUP

### 7.1 Timelines

| Data Category       | Retention Period     | Deletion Type        |
|---------------------|----------------------|----------------------|
| VoiceCommandHistory | 180 days             | Soft delete/anonymize|
| SavedDesign         | Permanent (unless removed by user) | User-controlled |
| Order Logs          | 7 years              | Legal record (hard)  |
| Audit Events        | 24 months            | Archival             |

### 7.2 Logging Security

- All access logged (device + IP)
- Pseudonymization on PII fallback tables
- Tamper-proof AuditLog structure  

---

## 8. OWNERSHIP & ACCESS CONTROL

| Entity              | Owner Role         | Editable By             | Readable By             |
|---------------------|--------------------|--------------------------|--------------------------|
| UserProfile         | user               | user, admin              | system, user             |
| Product             | vendor, admin      | CMS admin, vendor self   | all users                |
| VoiceCommandHistory | system             | voice_engine             | AI team, anonymized read |
| Orders              | user               | user, fulfillment admin  | payment system, user     |
| LegalRules          | compliance team    | legal staff              | all systems              |

---

## 9. DATA VALIDATION RULES

### 9.1 API Schemas

- Enforced via OpenAPI 3.1 spec
- Type validation on every submitted field
- Range tests on decimals
- Regex test for email/enum fields

### 9.2 Frontend Forms

- Client-side JSON schema validation (AJV)
- Real-time informative error messages
- Region-aware checks on strain/product visibility

---

## 10. COMPLIANCE MAPPINGS

| Data Element             | Regulatory Scope         | Handling                            |
|--------------------------|--------------------------|-------------------------------------|
| Email, Phone             | GDPR + CCPA              | Encrypted at REST, deletable        |
| Payment Data             | PCI-DSS Level 1          | Tokenized via Stripe or equivalent  |
| Medical Use Strings      | HIPAA-Adjacent           | Unlinked from personal identities   |
| Voice Recordings         | Custom T&C Consent       | Optional logging; user-deletable    |
| Regional Access Logs     | Legal Audit Trail        | Secure, expirable via jurisdiction  |

---

## 11. DATA DELIVERY & IMPORT FORMATS

| Module                     | Format            | Direction | Purpose                            |
|----------------------------|-------------------|-----------|------------------------------------|
| Product Catalog Import     | CSV / XLSX        | Import    | Vendor product onboarding          |
| SavedDesign Export         | JSON / STL / .glb | Export    | Share or 3DPoD printout            |
| Strain Directory Sync      | JSON API          | Import    | Scheduled external updates         |
| Voice Command Archive      | CSV / JSONL       | Export    | Logs for training or audit         |

---

## 12. APPENDICES

### 12.1 Reference Taxonomy Endpoints
- `/taxonomies/guru-personas`
- `/taxonomies/strain-effects`
- `/taxonomies/shop-categories`

### 12.2 Public-Facing Data Dictionaries  
- `/docs/datadict/v1.json`  
- `/openapi/ganjaguru.yaml`

---

**End of Document**

ğŸª 3D Navigation Prototype: Gravity-Gone UI
Concept: Replace traditional menus and scrolling with a physics-based, spatial, orbital interface where users move between floating â€œislandsâ€ (modules) like celestial bodiesâ€”using drag, gesture, or voice commands. Think: Mario Galaxy meets Snoop Doggâ€™s strain map inside a VR hotbox.

ğŸ§² Movement Physics Details
Element
Description
Inertia Drag
After user stops dragging/scrolling, the view continues gliding until it gently slows down.
Snapping Gravity Field
Islands have low-level magnetic pull. As user drifts nearby, the view snaps toward the center of an islandâ€™s â€œgravity zoneâ€ (optional override).
Collision Avoidance
Islands auto-repel to avoid overlap. Use bounding spheres for spatial awareness.
Hover Feedback
Mouse hover = island glow + tooltip. Voice hover = icon pulse.

// Orbital Camera Controller
function moveToIsland(islandName) {
Â Â const target = getIslandCoordinates(islandName);
Â Â gsap.to(camera.position, {
Â Â Â Â x: target.x,
Â Â Â Â y: target.y,
Â Â Â Â z: target.z,
Â Â Â Â duration: 2,
Â Â Â Â ease: "power2.inOut"
Â Â });
}

// Scroll Inertia (pseudo)
let scrollVelocity = 0;
onScroll(event) {
Â Â scrollVelocity += event.deltaY * 0.01;
}
updateLoop() {
Â Â camera.rotation.y += scrollVelocity;
Â Â scrollVelocity *= 0.95; // friction
}

# Gravity-Gone Web Outline & Layout Concept

## 1. Structure (Outline) â€“ Breaking the Mold

### Non-Linear Navigation
- **Concept**: Users land anywhere and navigate freely without a traditional homepage.

### Dynamic Entry Points
- **Implementation**: Real-time interactive portals based on user behavior.

### Modular Shifting
- **Design**: Floating islands(GanjaGuru island, strain creation studio island, 3DPoD and POD e-commerce that uses AR and VR island, grow area creation studio with AR and VR) that respond to user interactions.

---

## 2. Layout (Visual Arrangement) â€“ Gravity Defying

### Floating Elements
- **Functionality**: Content, buttons, and images drift, rotate, and hover dynamically.

### 3D Depth & Layering
- **Experience**: Elements exist in virtual depth, allowing users to "pull" or "push" sections.

### Orbital Navigation
- **Design**: Menus move in circular orbits instead of traditional navigation bars.

### Weightless Scrolling
- **Interaction**: Users "propel" themselves through content with space-like movement.

### Interactive Gravity Fields
- **User Engagement**: Users can interact with elements through gestures, cursor movement, or voice commands.

### Portal-Based Exploration
- **Navigation**: Users step into portals that transform into new pages(.

---

## 3. Key Features

### AI-Powered E-commerce
- **Concept**: A seamless, voice-controlled shopping experience for cannabis products.

### Dynamic Design Studio
- **Functionality**: 3DPoD and PoD with AR and VR integration for personalized product creation.

### Consultation Services
- **Options**: Virtual, video, and in-person consultations for cannabis-related designs.

### Eco-Friendly Products
- **Sourcing**: All products are sustainable and biodegradable, leveraging auto drop-shipping.

---

## 4. Color and Typography

### Color Palette
- **Theme**: Use marijuana colors with shades that invoke curiosity and a sense of purchasing. Use yellow and black and gold and silver and shading.

### Font Selection
- **Combination**: Utilize Futura, Jazzy, Pippin, Sans Serif, Times New Roman, and Montserrat for a unique look.

---

## 5. Technical Specifications

### Head Section
- Include:
Â Â - All SEO elements (meta tags, social media, schema)
Â Â - Font and animation and interactivity and button and library and script links
Â Â - Manifest and service worker links
Â Â - ARIA roles for accessibility
Â Â - Schema of all types
Â Â - Robo.txt
Â Â - security
Â Â - Service worker
Â Â - Llm, Ai/Ml, AR, VR, 3DPoD, PoD, e-commerce, nltk, voice scripts and libraries

### HTML Structure
- **Sections**:

Â Â - Header with its own border, strategically placed logo, multiple prominent CTAâ€™s(Take a Toke and Hold the Smoke), a centered H1, icons(voice, search, dark mode, account, language selection, cart, social media), interactive hamburger menu that only shows when clicked and or hovered over
Â Â - Video Hero with its own border
Â Â - Main Content with its own border
Â Â - Onboarding(interactive) with its own border
Â Â - What We Do with its own border
Â Â - About Us with its own border
Â Â - Services with its own border in 4 X 4 grid and each service having its own border and shadowing with seo
Â Â - How it works with its own border
Â Â - Download/Install/offline with its own border
Â Â - 3DPoD and PoD E-commerce with AR/VR with its own border
Â Â - Ride and Delivery Booking with its own border
Â Â - Blog with its own border
Â Â - Testimonials with its own border
Â Â - FAQs with its own border
Â Â - Features with its own border
Â Â - Team with its own border
Â Â - Gallery with its own border
Â Â - Help and support with its own border
Â Â - TOS/Privacy/Security with its own border
Â Â - Contact with its own border
Â Â - Footer with its own border

### Styling & Aesthetics
- **Borders**: Each section has its unique border and styling.
- **Animation**: Utilize interactivity, gamification, and animation for a dynamic feel.

---

## 6. Monetization Strategies
N
### Header Bidding, pragmatic advertising, PPV, pay per download & PPC
- Implement various advertising strategies to maximize revenue.

### User Engagement
- Create micro-interactions that enhance user experience and generate revenue.
