1. Data Acquisition and Sourcing
This phase focuses on identifying and collecting the necessary data to build and train the AI models.
 * Primary Data Sources:
   * User Interactions: Data generated from user conversations with the GanjaGuru AI, including questions asked, responses given, and user feedback. This is the most crucial source for refining the natural language processing (NLP) models.
   * Community Content: User-generated posts, comments, and interactions on the platform. This data can be used to understand trends, popular topics, and community-specific language.
   * Product Information: Data from partnering dispensaries and brands, including product descriptions, strain information (e.g., THC/CBD content, terpenes), and user reviews.
 * Secondary Data Sources:
   * Public Datasets: Open-source datasets related to cannabis science, regulations, and consumer trends.
   * Licensed Databases: Data from specialized databases or research firms that provide information on cannabis strains, medical research, and market analysis.
 * Data Collection Methods:
   * APIs: Use APIs from partners to pull in real-time product information and inventory data.
   * Web Scraping (if applicable): Systematically collect publicly available information on strains or market data, while ensuring compliance with legal and ethical guidelines.
   * In-App Analytics: Implement a robust analytics system to track user behavior, feature usage, and other engagement metrics.
2. Data Preparation and Organization
Once the data is acquired, it must be cleaned, structured, and organized to be usable for AI models. This is often the most time-consuming part of the process.
 * Data Cleaning:
   * De-duplication: Remove duplicate entries from product lists or community posts.
   * Handling Missing Values: Fill in missing data points (e.g., a strain with no terpene profile) or flag them for review.
   * Standardization: Ensure all data is in a consistent format (e.g., all dates are in the same format, all measurements use the same units).
   * Normalization: For conversational data, normalize text by converting it to lowercase, removing punctuation, and handling misspellings.
 * Data Labeling:
   * Conversation Tagging: Manually or semi-automatically label user questions and AI responses with "intents" (e.g., "product inquiry," "dosage question," "recreational use"). This is critical for training the voice intent handler and the main NLP model.
   * Content Categorization: Categorize community posts and product reviews by topic, sentiment, or other relevant tags.
 * Data Storage and Management:
   * Database: Use a scalable database (e.g., a NoSQL database like MongoDB for flexibility or a relational database like PostgreSQL for structured data) to store the raw and processed data.
   * Data Lake: Implement a data lake to store all raw, unstructured data from various sources. This allows for future analysis and use.
   * Data Pipeline: Set up an automated data pipeline using tools like Apache Airflow or Google Cloud Dataflow to handle the entire process from acquisition to storage.
3. Data Usage for AI Model Training and Refinement
This is the final phase where the prepared data is used to build and continuously improve the AI models.
 * Model Training:
   * NLP Models: Use the cleaned and labeled conversational data to train the natural language processing model for the GanjaGuru chatbot. This will enable it to understand and respond to a wide variety of user queries.
   * Recommendation Engine: Use product and user behavior data to train a recommendation engine that can suggest personalized strains, products, and content.
   * Image Recognition: Use the product and plant imagery to train a computer vision model for identifying strains and products through the AR/VR features.
 * Model Refinement and Iteration:
   * Continuous Learning: Implement a feedback loop where user interactions and feedback are used to continuously retrain and refine the models.
   * A/B Testing: Use A/B testing to evaluate different versions of the AI model to see which one performs better in a real-world setting.
   * Monitoring: Establish a system for monitoring model performance, accuracy, and fairness to ensure the AI remains effective and unbiased.  Here are the detailed plans for the remaining items needed for the GanjaGuru project:
AI Model Monitoring and Retraining
A robust plan for monitoring and retraining the AI models is essential to ensure they remain accurate and relevant as the market, regulations, and user behavior evolve.
Monitoring Strategy:
 * Performance Metrics: Continuously track key performance indicators (KPIs) for the AI models, such as accuracy of responses, relevance of recommendations, and the rate of user-reported errors.
 * Model Drift Detection: Implement a system to monitor for "model drift," which occurs when the real-world data and user interactions change over time, causing the model's predictions to become less accurate. This can be done by regularly comparing the model's performance on new data to its performance on the original training data.
 * Feedback Loop: Create an automated feedback loop where user interactions (e.g., "was this helpful?" buttons) and explicit feedback are collected and used to identify areas for model improvement.
 * Alert System: Set up an alert system that notifies the development team when a model's performance drops below a predefined threshold.
Retraining Strategy:
 * Scheduled Retraining: Establish a regular schedule (e.g., monthly or quarterly) for retraining the AI models with a fresh, updated dataset that includes the most recent user interactions and new product information.
 * Event-Triggered Retraining: In addition to scheduled retraining, trigger an ad-hoc retraining session when a significant change occurs, such as a major regulatory update, a new product line, or a sudden change in user behavior.
 * Human-in-the-Loop: Incorporate a "human-in-the-loop" process where human experts review a sample of the model's responses and feedback to guide the retraining process and ensure the quality and safety of the model's output.
Data Governance Policy
A formal data governance policy will ensure that all data is handled ethically, securely, and in compliance with all relevant privacy regulations.
Key Components of the Policy:
 * Data Privacy: A strict policy on user data privacy, including data anonymization and pseudonymization to protect user identities. The policy must comply with regulations like GDPR and CCPA.
 * Data Security: A detailed plan for data security, including encryption of all data at rest and in transit, access controls to limit who can view sensitive data, and regular security audits.
 * Ethical AI Principles: A set of ethical guidelines for the AI models to prevent bias, ensure fairness in recommendations, and maintain transparency in how the AI works.
 * Data Ownership and Usage: Clear rules on who owns the data and how it can be used. The policy should specify that user data will not be sold to third parties without explicit consent.
 * Regulatory Compliance: A commitment to staying up-to-date with all local, state, and federal cannabis regulations that may affect data collection and usage.
Scalable Cloud Infrastructure
A scalable and robust cloud infrastructure is the backbone of the GanjaGuru project, allowing it to grow from a small user base to a large, global community.
Infrastructure Requirements:
 * Cloud Provider: Select a reliable cloud provider like AWS, Google Cloud Platform, or Microsoft Azure. The choice should be based on scalability, cost, and the specific AI and machine learning tools they offer.
 * Scalable Architecture: Implement a microservices architecture that allows different components of the application (e.g., the chatbot, the database, the AR/VR features) to scale independently.
 * Load Balancing: Use load balancers to distribute user traffic evenly across multiple servers, preventing the application from crashing under heavy load.
 * Auto-Scaling: Configure auto-scaling rules to automatically add or remove server resources based on user demand, ensuring high availability and cost efficiency.
 * AI/ML Services: Utilize the cloud provider's managed AI/ML services (e.g., Amazon SageMaker, Google AI Platform) to simplify the deployment, monitoring, and retraining of the AI models.
 * Content Delivery Network (CDN): Use a CDN to cache content (e.g., images, 3D models) and deliver it to users quickly, regardless of their geographical location.
Beta Testing Program
A structured beta testing program will provide invaluable feedback from early users, helping to refine the application and gather testimonials for the public launch.
Program Plan:
 * Recruitment: Recruit a diverse group of users who match the target demographic to participate in the beta test. This can be done through social media, email newsletters, and targeted advertising.
 * Testing Phases:
   * Alpha Phase: Internal testing with employees and close partners to identify major bugs and issues.
   * Closed Beta Phase: Invite a small, select group of external users to test the core features and provide feedback through surveys and interviews.
   * Open Beta Phase: Gradually open the beta to a larger group of users, allowing for a wider range of feedback and stress-testing the infrastructure.
 * Feedback Mechanism: Provide an easy-to-use in-app feedback tool and a dedicated channel (e.g., a Slack group or Discord server) for testers to report bugs and share their thoughts.
 * Incentives: Offer incentives to beta testers, such as early access to new features, premium subscriptions, or GanjaGuru-branded merchandise, to encourage participation and detailed feedback.
 * Testimonial Collection: At the end of the beta period, ask satisfied testers for testimonials and quotes that can be used in the launch marketing campaign. 
Go-to-Market Plan
A comprehensive go-to-market plan will guide the launch and initial growth of GanjaGuru.
1. Target Audience:
 * Demographics: Adults in legal cannabis markets, ages 25-45, interested in wellness, technology, and conscious cannabis consumption.
 * Psychographics: Tech-savvy individuals who value education, discretion, and community, and who may feel overwhelmed by the complexity of the cannabis market.
2. Core Messaging:
 * Unique Value Proposition (UVP): "Your personal, AI-powered cannabis companion for education, discovery, and community."
 * Slogan: "GanjaGuru: Cannabis, demystified."
 * Key Benefits: Personalized recommendations, discreet and private assistance, engaging community, and access to accurate, up-to-date information.
3. Marketing Channels:
 * Content Marketing: Create blog posts, videos, and social media content focused on cannabis education, strain reviews, and wellness.
 * Social Media: Use platforms like Instagram, TikTok, and relevant subreddits to build a community and create engaging, educational content. Partner with cannabis influencers and content creators.
 * Paid Advertising: Run targeted digital ad campaigns on platforms that allow cannabis-related advertising, focusing on non-promotional, educational content.
 * Public Relations: Pitch GanjaGuru to tech, wellness, and cannabis-focused publications. Issue a press release about the launch, highlighting the innovative use of AI and AR/VR.
4. Launch Strategy:
 * Pre-Launch: Run a viral marketing campaign to build a waitlist. Offer early access to the beta program as an incentive.
 * Launch Day: Go live with the application and a coordinated marketing push across all channels.
 * Post-Launch: Continuously monitor user feedback and analytics. Implement a growth hacking strategy to drive user acquisition and retention through features like referral programs.
Customer Support Plan
A plan for customer support is critical for building trust and ensuring user satisfaction.
1. Help Center:
 * Create a comprehensive help center with a searchable knowledge base of FAQs, tutorials, and articles on how to use the app's features.
 * The help center should also include a section on safety, privacy, and community guidelines.
2. Ticketing System:
 * Implement a ticketing system (e.g., Zendesk, HubSpot) to manage user inquiries and issues.
 * Users can submit tickets for technical problems, billing questions, or to report a bug or a community guideline violation.
 * All tickets should be prioritized and routed to the appropriate team member.
3. Support Team:
 * Hire and train a small, dedicated support team to respond to user inquiries.
 * Support agents should be knowledgeable about the application, its features, and the community guidelines.
 * Implement a system for tracking support metrics, such as response time and resolution rate.
Performance Metrics (KPIs)
Defining key performance indicators (KPIs) will allow the GanjaGuru team to measure success and make data-driven decisions.
 * User Acquisition:
   * Cost Per Acquisition (CPA): How much it costs to acquire a new user.
   * User Growth Rate: The rate at which new users are joining the platform.
 * User Engagement:
   * Daily/Monthly Active Users (DAU/MAU): The number of unique users who engage with the app on a daily or monthly basis.
   * Session Length: The average time a user spends in the app per session.
   * Feature Adoption: The percentage of users who use key features like GuruChat, the AR/VR tools, or the community forums.
 * User Retention:
   * Churn Rate: The percentage of users who stop using the app over a given period.
   * Retention Cohorts: Tracking the behavior of user groups (cohorts) over time to see how they retain.
Legal and Compliance
Maintaining a strong legal and compliance framework is non-negotiable for a project in the cannabis space.
1. EULA and Privacy Policy:
 * End-User License Agreement (EULA): A legal document that outlines the terms of service for the application. It should cover user responsibilities, intellectual property rights, disclaimers, and dispute resolution.
 * Privacy Policy: A clear and easy-to-understand document that informs users exactly what data is being collected, why it's being collected, how it's being used, and with whom it might be shared. It must also detail how users can access, correct, or delete their data.
 * Third-Party Review: Both documents must be reviewed by legal counsel specializing in both technology and cannabis law to ensure they are legally sound and enforceable.
2. State-Specific Compliance:
 * Continuous Monitoring: Establish a dedicated process for continuously monitoring changes in cannabis regulations at the local, state, and federal levels. This could involve subscribing to legal news services or using an AI-powered compliance tool.
 * Compliance Team: Assign a person or a small team to be responsible for staying on top of regulatory changes and translating those changes into actionable updates for the application.
 * Dynamic Content: Design the application to be flexible enough to dynamically adapt to different state regulations. For example, the app could automatically adjust purchase limits or display state-specific advertising warnings based on the user's location.
 * Legal Counsel: Maintain a relationship with cannabis law firms to provide ongoing guidance and review of new features, marketing campaigns, and business partnerships to ensure everything remains compliant. Plan for Continuous Competitive Analysis
A continuous competitive analysis plan is essential for GanjaGuru to maintain its market leadership. This plan should be a dynamic process, not a one-time event.
1. Identify and Monitor Competitors:
 * Direct Competitors: Identify companies that offer similar AI-powered cannabis assistance, educational content, or community features.
 * Indirect Competitors: Also monitor broader wellness apps, cannabis social networks, and review sites that could be competing for the same user base.
 * Monitoring Tools: Use tools like a competitive intelligence platform, social media listening tools, and Google Alerts to track competitor updates, product changes, and media mentions.
2. Analyze Competitor Strategies:
 * Product Features: Regularly assess new features or updates launched by competitors. This includes everything from new AI capabilities to changes in their user interface or content.
 * Marketing and Messaging: Analyze competitor marketing campaigns, social media content, and branding. This helps to identify what resonates with users and what new angles can be explored.
 * Pricing Models: Track any changes to competitor pricing, subscription plans, or monetization strategies.
 * User Feedback: Read user reviews on app stores, social media, and forums to understand what users like and dislike about competing products. This provides invaluable insights into pain points that GanjaGuru can address.
3. Internal Strategy and Adaptation:
 * Regular Reporting: Create a system for regular reporting (e.g., a monthly competitive analysis report) that is shared with the product, marketing, and leadership teams.
 * Strategic Response: Based on the analysis, the team should collaboratively decide on a strategic response. This could involve prioritizing new features, adjusting the marketing message, or exploring new partnerships.
 * Market Trends: Monitor the broader cannabis and AI industries for emerging trends. For example, if a new type of cannabinoid becomes popular or a new AI technology becomes available, GanjaGuru should be prepared to adapt.

## I. Home Portal: The Cosmic Entry Point

### Wireframe Overview

- **Visual Setting:**  
  A cosmic, star-dense void sets the background. Center stage floats an anthropomorphic, luminous cannabis goddess (feminine Groot vibe), gently animatedâ€”her leaves rustle, her chest rises and falls with a living, plantlike breath.

- **Hero Animation:**  
  When she exhales, a swirling spiral of vapor uncoils, filling mid-screen. As the smoke forms, glowing, retro-futuristic â€œThe GanjaGuruâ€ logo text emerges holographically inside the swirl, gently pulsing with the breath animation.

### Orbital Navigation Menu

- **Menu Architecture:**  
  Six iconic, low-poly, softly glowing 3D icons orbit the figure horizontallyâ€”always in slow, elliptical motion. Icon set: Home (house), Shop (cart), Design (gear or beaker), Learn (leaf + book/mortarboard), Community (speech bubble or people), Account (crescent profile silhouette).

- **Animation States:**
  - **Idle:** Icons pulse, orbit smoothly. Mini-lens flares drift over icon surfaces.
  - **Approach (Cursor/Touch):** Orbital motion slows near the cursor/finger. The closest icon glows, grows (by 30%), casting a brighter â€œhalo.â€
  - **Hover:** Orbit freezes. The active icon floats out, grows to 150% scale with a gentle bounce, and a label (e.g., â€œE-commerce Sectionâ€) fades in below.
  - **Haptic Feedback (Mobile):** A gentle, single vibration triggers as the icon growsâ€”signaling "ready to select."
  - **Select:** When tapped/clicked, the icon fills the screen with a radial expansion, background visually zooming in toward it (â€œweightless scrollingâ€ effect), then fades to initiate the floating island transition.

## II. Floating Islands: Modular Content Universes

### Wireframe Overview

- **Spatial Design:**  
  The selected â€œislandâ€ (e.g., Shop) floats into center viewâ€”a semi-translucent, multi-level 3D platform with specified shadows and depth. The backgroundâ€™s infinite starfield drifts gently, maintaining the sensation of movement and infinity.

- **Layout Structure:**
  - **Modular Content Blocks:** Each island contains flexible, card-like content modules (e.g., categories, featured items, search). Modules have subtle 3D elevationâ€”casting soft, colored shadows and glows.
  - **Visual Effects:** Layers move at different speeds (parallax), foreground elements â€œbobâ€ and â€œrotateâ€ as if on water or drifting in spaceâ€”especially in reaction to scrolling or flicks.
  - **Physics-Based Scrolling:** There is no scrollbar. A gentle scroll launches the entire island in a smooth, inertia-based driftâ€”the further/faster you scroll, the more momentum, until â€œgravityâ€ friction slows and stops it. Snappy, elastic â€œbounceâ€ when you hit the content boundary.

### Prototype Flows & Animations

- **Entry Animation:**  
  As the island loads, it â€œfloatsâ€ in from the side (direction = original orbital path of the selected icon). Background starfield moves slightly faster for the first second, delivering sensation of â€œapproach.â€ Main content rises from the island surface, with top-to-bottom or left-right stagger.

- **Scroll/Drift:**  
  - **Mouse Wheel/Flick:** The whole island drifts in scroll direction. If the user scrolls, cards and images within gently sway, lagging behind then catching up for that zero-G, inertia illusion.
  - **Mobile â€œPull/Pushâ€ Gestures:** Two-finger pinch shrinks the island (zooms out), revealing adjoining islands in the cosmic sea. Pinch-out or tap on a distant island immediately â€œzoomsâ€ it to the center, with a warp-speed, parallax transition.

- **Item Interactions:**
  - **Hover on Card:** The product block grows, glows, product image does a lazy 360Â° rotate. Background gently darkens to spotlight active block.
  - **Click for Details:** A â€œsub-islandâ€ (smaller, leveled up from the main island surface) floats forward, dimming/blurring the main background. This contains details/reviews/tools for the selected item. Push away (back/dismiss) with the same drifting, fade-out animation.

- **Micro-interactions:**
  - **Floating Badges:** As a user earns XP, activates coupons, or gets AI suggestions, badges or animated orbs float in, bounce once, and gently snap to an â€œachievement railâ€ on the islandâ€™s edge.
  - **Haptic (Mobile):** Every successful add-to-cart or snap action is paired with a pleasant, short vibration; drag-and-drop is accompanied by a soft, continuous rumble.

## III. Design & Crafting Island â€“ The Creator's Crucible

### Wireframe Overview

- **Environment:**  
  The floating island now floats above a semitransparent, gridded digital board (workshop look), with faint animated glows marking snapping points.

- **Central Focus:**  
  In the middle, a fully rotatable, zoom-friendly 3D cannabis item (e.g., bong) is showcasedâ€”built of modular parts.

- **Panels:**
  - **Left:** Palette of modular pieces, each glowing gentlyâ€”drag-and-droppable.
  - **Right:** Customization tools: color swatches, material shifters (sliders), pattern selectors.

### Prototype Flows & Animations

- **Drag-and-Drop:**  
  User drags a component from the palette; as it nears a snap point, a magnetic-like glow appears, the piece animates in and fits perfectly. The interface gives a tap-like vibration (mobile) and a bright pulse effect at the snap point.
- **Real-Time Changes:**  
  All edits update the 3D render live. Colors and textures shift gradually to show physicality (no harsh switches).
- **Shape Manipulation:**  
  Dragging on a model part (neck, base, etc.) stretches or shrinks itâ€”component geometry animates smoothly, and the price/materials panel updates with a pop.
- **AR/VR Preview:**  
  Tap â€œView in My Space.â€ The screen wipes to live camera mode (mobile/tablet), overlaying the 3D model onto the scene. Pinch/rotate gestures resize or spin the item live.

## IV. Cross-Sectional Navigation â€“ The Stonerverse Map

### Wireframe Overview

- **Cosmic Map:**  
  In a fixed, corner-floating panel, a mini version of the entire â€œislandsâ€ constellation: all available sections (Shop, Design, Learn, Community, etc.) represented as floating, glowing spheres. The userâ€™s current zone is highlighted and gently pulsating. Active islands float forward; others drift in the periphery.

  Thin, glowing Bezier lines link previous steps, showing navigation history as a constellation path.
- **Back/Home Button:**  
  A simple, circular embossed GanjaGuru logo sits unobtrusively (low opacity). Tap/click reverses your last moveâ€”current island shrinks and floats away, the cosmic void zooms back out, and the next nearest island or home portal floats in naturally.

## Deep Dive: Animated, Responsive, and Personalized Portals

- **Dynamic Entry:**  
  Users are not dropped staticallyâ€”every entry is loaded via a swirling nebula or energy field animation, personalized by query, location, or referral.
- **Real-Time AI Guidance:**  
  If an Oklahoma user lands and needs OMMA advice, the portal animates in green/gold, branding the section as â€œOklahoma Dashboard.â€ If a user comes for â€œbest strains for sleep,â€ theyâ€™re floated seamlessly into â€œMedical/Effectsâ€ shop islands, with the corresponding UI ring glowing blue as navigation feedback.
- **Interest-based Surfing:**  
  Hovering/lingering near certain islands causes the AI to float in â€œsuggested next islandsâ€ around the peripheryâ€”each previewing a quick highlight. Frequent use customizes the predicted paths for each user.

## Physics, Animation, and Haptic Feedback: The â€œZero Gravityâ€ Experience

- **Autonomous Floating:**  
  Island modules are never static: they all exhibit slight â€œidleâ€ drift, compass-like rotations, and slow up/down bobbing (Â±5px) to evoke constant motion, using Perlin noise or spring-based animation.
- **Inertia & Momentum:**  
  Flicked or flung islands carry velocity based on input power; they â€œslideâ€ to rest, occasionally gently bouncing on boundaries.
- **Snap & Cluster:**  
  Drag an island near another (on wide screens): it snaps into a â€œmagnetizedâ€ cluster with a pulsing glow and subtle sound cue (or haptic tap).
- **Pull/Push Gestures:**  
  Mouse or two-finger pan slides the view sideways/across, feeling like youâ€™re peering around asteroids in space. Restoring to default focus allows the islands to â€œgravitateâ€ back into alignment.
- **Haptic Language:**  
  - Every snap: short, crisp buzz.
  - Snap + completion (e.g., design attached): two quick pulses.
  - Sculpting/dragging: continuous soft rumble, fading on release.
- **Detail Interactivity:**  
  - Hover/click: gentle glow pulse and subtle size â€œbounce.â€
  - AR: Place/Move item = soft double tap.

## Narrative: User Journey Example

1. **Portal Entry:**  
   User lands in the cosmic void, greeted by the living â€œGanjaGuruâ€ plant avatar, with orbiting navigation pulsing.
2. **Menu Selection:**  
   Icons slow and respond as the user hovers Shop, which pops out; select itâ€”weightless zoom carries user into the floating Shop island.
3. **Zero-G Browsing:**  
   The new island drifts into place, contents bob and sway. User flick-scrolls through goodsâ€”items gently lag and float.
4. **Engage:**  
   Hovering over a product, it rotates/wobbles. Tapping expands a sub-island. All animations use momentum and inertia; nothing â€œsnapsâ€ harshly.
5. **Navigate Home:**  
   User pinches to â€œzoom out,â€ revealing the stonerverse map, floats to Design island, drops a new session.
6. **Physicality:**  
   Every snap, drop, add-to-cart includes haptic pulses on mobile, visual pulses on desktop.
7. **Exit:**  
   User returns via the floating logoâ€”reverse drift animation returns them to the cosmic home.

## Core Takeaways for Designers & Devs

- **Every action feels alive, fluid, and cosmic.**
- **Navigation isnâ€™t a sequenceâ€”itâ€™s orientation and movement, always expressing user position/context.**
- **Physics-based scrolling, parallax, haptic feedback, and animated micro-responses make the interface a place to explore, not just click.**
- **Responsiveness and accessibility are layered in: hover/selection magnifies objects, ARIA announces focus state, haptic/vibration output confirms actions.**
- **User journey is as much about the journey as the destination: every transition is transportive, every island its own world.**

## Components:

### 1.1. Avatar Library

# 1. AI Ethics & Governance Framework Document

## Title  
**GanjaGuru AI Ethics and Governance Framework**

## Objective  
To establish responsible, transparent, and accountable use of AI across the GanjaGuru platform with emphasis on ethical alignment, compliance, and user trust.

## Components

### 1.1. Ethical Principles  
- Autonomy: Respect user control over personal data and preferences.  
- Non-maleficence: Prevent harm and bias in AI outputs.  
- Justice: Ensure fairness and inclusivity in AI recommendations and content.  
- Beneficence: Promote user well-being and positive social outcomes.  
- Transparency: Explain AI-driven decisions clearly to users.  
- Accountability: Define roles and responsibilities for AI outcomes and data governance.

### 1.2. Explainability & Transparency  
- Implement explainable AI tools showing why suggestions or decisions were made.  
- Provide users with accessible logs of AI interactions and data use.

### 1.3. Bias Mitigation  
- Regular audits for bias in strain recommendations, growth tips, chatbot responses.  
- Diverse training data representing different geographies, demographics, and cannabis culture.

### 1.4. Data Privacy & Security  
- Compliance with GDPR, CCPA, HIPAA (where applicable).  
- Consent management, anonymization, minimal data retention.  
- Secure AI model training pipelines with encrypted data stores and access controls.

### 1.5. AI Oversight & Monitoring  
- Establish an AI Ethics Board (internal and external experts) reviewing AI impact and complaints.  
- Real-time monitoring dashboards for AI performance and fairness.  
- Human-in-the-loop escalation for sensitive or disputed cases.

### 1.6. Regulatory Alignment  
- Continuous compliance checks with emerging AI laws (EU AI Act, US frameworks).  
- Documentation and certification aligned with industry recognized AI governance standards.

### 1.7. User Control & Feedback  
- User interfaces to manage AI personalization settings.  
- Feedback channels for users to report AI errors or offensive outputs.

### 4.2. Content Caching  
- Service Workers caching critical modules, FAQs, user history, recent product catalogs.  
- Pre-download option for tutorials, chat histories, and shopping carts.

### 4.3. Offline Chat Support  
- Local LLM embeddings with intent fallback for offline query answering.  
- Queue outbound user requests for sync on reconnect.

### 4.4. Bandwidth Detection & Adaptive Streaming  
- Switch AR/VR and video content quality dynamically.  
- Defer non-essential updates and ads in low bandwidth.

1. As a first-time user

,





I want to ask the GanjaGuru for a strain suggestion based on how I feel,

So that I can elevate my mood and have a meaningful experience.

User inputs mood or intention (via text or emoji/mood slider).
Guru responds with 1â€“3 personalized strain recommendations.
Strain profiles include effects, terpene content, and ritual pairing.
User can save suggestion, explore ritual, or request a new match.

So that I can integrate cannabis into my wellness practice.

Personalized to user SoulPrint (time, mood history, recent intentions).
Completion unlocks reflection prompt and badge progress.

,

User confirms match or flags uncertainty.

ğŸ”Š 

4. As a hands-free user

,

Data updates live with each new interaction.
User can annotate, favorite, or export entries.









ğŸ†

,

So that I feel motivated to deepen my journey.

Here is a comprehensive, advanced, and developer-focused set of technical documentation components for the **GanjaGuru** platform covering API Documentation, SDK Documentation, and Technical Guides as requested.

# ğŸ“˜ GanjaGuru Technical and Developer Documentation

## 1. API Documentation

### 1.1 Authentication

- **Method:** Bearer Token in `Authorization` header  
- **Header example:**  
  `Authorization: Bearer YOUR_API_KEY`  
- **How to Obtain API Key:**  
  From user account settings under **API Keys** or generated via secure admin panel.  
- **Security Notes:**  
  Use HTTPS for all API requests. Refresh and revoke tokens as needed.

### 1.2 Base URL

- Production: `https://api.ganjaguru.com/v1`  
- Sandbox: `https://sandbox.api.ganjaguru.com/v1`

### 1.3 Endpoints Overview

| Endpoint                        | Method | Description                              | Request Body / Query                      | Response Summary                |
|--------------------------------|--------|------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------|-------------------------------|
| `/users`                       | GET    | List users with filtering                  | Query params: `region`, `role`, `status`| Paginated user list             |
| `/users/{user_id}`             | GET    | Get user profile                            | N/A                                      | User profile JSON              |
| `/users/{user_id}`             | PATCH  | Update user profile                         | JSON body with updatable fields          | Updated user profile           |
| `/products`                   | GET    | Retrieve product catalog                     | Query filters: `category`, `price_range`, `in_stock` | List of products              |
| `/products/{product_id}`       | GET    | Get detailed product info                    | N/A                                      | Product data with AR model URLs|
| `/orders`                    | POST   | Create a new order                           | Order details JSON (user, items, payment info) | Confirmation with order ID   |
| `/orders/{order_id}`          | GET    | Retrieve order status and details            | N/A                                      | Order status and tracking     |
| `/strains`                   | GET    | Retrieve cannabis strain catalog              | Query filters: `effects`, `genetics`     | Strain list                   |
| `/voice/commands`              | POST   | Submit voice command data for processing     | Audio or transcript payload               | Parsed intent and response    |
| `/designs`                   | GET    | Get user saved designs                         | Query param: `user_id`                     | List of design metadata       |
| `/designs/{design_id}`          | GET    | Get specific saved design metadata             | N/A                                      | Full design details           |

### 1.4 Request and Response Formats

- All requests and responses use **JSON** unless noted.  
- Pagination via `limit` and `offset` query parameters.  
- Example:  
  ```http
  GET /products?category=flower&in_stock=true&limit=20 HTTP/1.1
  Host: api.ganjaguru.com
  Authorization: Bearer YOUR_API_KEY
  Accept: application/json
  ```

### 1.5 Errors and Status Codes

- **200 OK:** Success  
- **201 Created:** Resource created  
- **400 Bad Request:** Missing or invalid parameters  
- **401 Unauthorized:** Missing or invalid API key  
- **403 Forbidden:** Access denied  
- **404 Not Found:** Resource not found  
- **500 Internal Server Error:** Unexpected failure

## 2. SDK Documentation

### 2.1 SDK Overview

GanjaGuru provides SDKs in JavaScript, Python, and mobile platforms (iOS and Android) to simplify API integration, handle authentication, and implement event-based interactions.

### 2.2 JavaScript SDK (npm Package: `ganjaguru-sdk`)

#### Installation

```bash
npm install ganjaguru-sdk
```

#### Initialization

```javascript
import GanjaGuruApi from 'ganjaguru-sdk';

const api = new GanjaGuruApi({ apiKey: 'YOUR_API_KEY' });
```

#### Fetch Products Example

```javascript
(async () => {
  const products = await api.getProducts({ category: 'flower', limit: 10 });
  console.log(products);
})();
```

#### Order Creation Example

```javascript
const order = await api.createOrder({
  userId: 'user-uuid',
  items: [{ productId: 'prod-uuid', quantity: 2 }],
  paymentMethod: 'stripe-token',
});
console.log(order.status);
```

### 2.3 Python SDK (Package: `ganjaguru`)

#### Installation

```bash
pip install ganjaguru
```

#### Initialization

```python
from ganjaguru import GanjaGuruApi

api = GanjaGuruApi(api_key='YOUR_API_KEY')
```

#### Get User Profile

```python
profile = api.get_user('user-uuid')
print(profile['display_name'])
```

#### Design Upload Example

```python
new_design = api.create_design(user_id='user-uuid', design_data={'product_base': 'bong', 'components_used': ['part1','part2']})
print(new_design['design_id'])
```

### 2.4 Mobile SDKs

- **iOS:** CocoaPods package `GanjaGuruSDK`  
- **Android:** Maven package `com.ganjaguru:sdk`  
- Common features: Authentication, Voice API wrapper, AR preview support, Floating islands state manager

## 3. Technical Guides

### 3.1 Architecture Overview  

- **Frontend:** React + Three.js for 3D and orbital navigation, Redux for state management, WebXR for AR integration, Web Speech API + Whisper for voice.  
- **Backend:** Node.js microservices, GraphQL API gateway, Firebase real-time database for chat and IoT device sync, serverless functions for AI inference and personalization.  
- **Data Layer:** PostgreSQL with JSONB for flexible content storage, Redis caching, Elasticsearch for search and recommendation indexing.

### 3.2 Data Flow

- **User Interaction:** Events captured on frontend â†’ API calls â†’ Backend microservices â†’ AI Personalization Engine â†’ Response rendered on frontend.  
- **Voice Command Handling:**  
  Audio input passed to Whisper-based ASR â†’ NLP intent extracted via fine-tuned LLM â†’ Intent sent to chatbot or UI navigation module.  
- **Order Processing:** Checkout data flows from frontend â†’ payment gateway (Stripe/WalletConnect) â†’ Order fulfillment microservice â†’ Vendor API notifications â†’ Delivery tracking updates.

### 3.3 API Protocols and Security

- HTTPS only communication  
- OAuth 2.0 Bearer tokens for authentication  
- Rate limiting per IP and per API key to prevent abuse  
- JSON Web Tokens (JWT) used for user session authorization  
- CORS enabled with strict origin whitelisting  

### 3.4 Deployment and CI/CD

- Automated deployments via GitHub Actions  
- Unit and integration tests run on all branches  
- Canary releases for feature rollouts  
- AWS/GCP multi-region deployments with Kubernetes orchestration

### 3.5 Common Use Cases

| Use Case                   | Steps Involved                                | APIs/SDK Components                |
|----------------------------|-----------------------------------------------|----------------------------------|
| User Registration          | API key generation, profile creation           | `/users`, SDK auth module        |
| Product Browsing           | Filtering, sorting, AR preview                  | `/products`, SDK getProducts      |
| Voice-Activated Navigation | Voice command capture, NLP intent routing      | `/voice/commands`, SDK voice API  |
| Custom Design Creation     | Drag/drop modular parts, save design metadata  | `/designs`, SDK design module     |
| Order Placement & Tracking | Cart management, checkout, real-time updates   | `/orders`, SDK order management   |

# GanjaGuru Security Policy

## 1. Purpose  
To protect GanjaGuruâ€™s platform, infrastructure, and user data through comprehensive security measures.

## 2. Scope  
Applies to all users, employees, contractors, and third parties interacting with GanjaGuru systems.

## 3. Security Principles  
- **Confidentiality:** Ensure only authorized access to sensitive data.  
- **Integrity:** Data is accurate and unaltered except by authorized processes.  
- **Availability:** Systems and data are available when needed.

## 4. Data Protection Measures  
- Encryption of sensitive data at rest and in transit (TLS 1.2+).  
- Use of secure authentication protocols and multi-factor authentication for employees and admin access.  
- Regular security patches, vulnerability scanning, and penetration testing.  
- Secure software development lifecycle practices including code reviews and automated testing.

## 5. Access Control  
- Role-based access limiting data and system access.  
- Logging of all access attempts and administrative actions.  
- Periodic review and revocation of unnecessary access.

## 6. Incident Response  
- Incident detection and alerting systems in place.  
- Defined incident response plan including containment, investigation, notification, and mitigation steps.  
- User notification in case of data breaches when legally required.

## 7. Compliance  
- Adherence to GDPR, CCPA, HIPAA (as applicable), PCI DSS, and other relevant standards.  
- Regular audits and compliance reviews.

## 8. User Responsibilities  
- Protect your account credentials.  
- Report suspicious activity promptly.

## 9. Physical Security  
- Data centers with controlled physical access.  
- Redundancy and disaster recovery mechanisms.

## 10. Policy Updates  
This Security Policy is reviewed and updated regularly to address emerging threats.
